<tr>
<th scope="row">Previous post</th>

<ul>
<li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Catholic_Church_sidebar" title="Template:Catholic Church sidebar"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Catholic_Church_sidebar" title="Template talk:Catholic Church sidebar"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li>
<li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Catholic_Church_sidebar&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li>
</ul>

<p><b>Pope Francis</b> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <span lang="la" xml:lang="la"><i>Franciscus</i></span>; <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>: <span lang="it" xml:lang="it"><i>Francesco</i></span>; <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <span lang="es" xml:lang="es"><i>Francisco</i></span>; born <b>Jorge Mario Bergoglio</b>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[b]</a></sup> 17 December 1936) is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_popes" title="List of popes">266th</a> and current <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Pope</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Courtesy_title" title="Courtesy title">title</a> he holds <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ex_officio" title="Ex officio">ex officio</a></i> as <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Rome" title="Diocese of Rome">Bishop of Rome</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereigns_of_Vatican_City_State" title="List of sovereigns of Vatican City State">sovereign</a> of <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a>. He chose Francis as his <a href="/wiki/Papal_name" title="Papal name">papal name</a> in honor of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Francis_of_Assisi" title="Saint Francis of Assisi">Saint Francis of Assisi</a>. Francis is the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit" title="Jesuit">Jesuit</a> pope, the first from the Americas, the first from the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a> and the first pope from outside Europe since Syrian <a href="/wiki/Pope_Gregory_III" title="Pope Gregory III">Gregory III</a>, who died in 741.</p>
<p>Born in <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, Argentina, Bergoglio worked briefly as a <a href="/wiki/Chemical_technologist" title="Chemical technologist">chemical technologist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bouncer_(doorman)" title="Bouncer (doorman)">nightclub bouncer</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[2]</a></sup> before beginning <a href="/wiki/Seminary" title="Seminary">seminary</a> studies. He was ordained a <a href="/wiki/Priesthood_(Catholic_Church)" title="Priesthood (Catholic Church)">Catholic priest</a> in 1969, and from 1973 to 1979 was Argentina's <a href="/wiki/Provincial_superior" title="Provincial superior">provincial superior</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Society of Jesus</a>. He was accused of handing two priests to the <a href="/wiki/National_Reorganization_Process" title="National Reorganization Process">National Reorganization Process</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Dirty_War" title="Dirty War">Dirty War</a>. He became the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Buenos_Aires" title="Archbishop of Buenos Aires">Archbishop of Buenos Aires</a> in 1998, and was created a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardinal_(Catholicism)" title="Cardinal (Catholicism)">cardinal</a> in 2001 by <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a>. He led the Argentine Church during the <a href="/wiki/December_2001_riots_in_Argentina" title="December 2001 riots in Argentina">December 2001 riots in Argentina</a>, and the administrations of <a href="/wiki/N%C3%A9stor_Kirchner" title="Néstor Kirchner">Néstor Kirchner</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Kirchner" title="Cristina Fernández de Kirchner">Cristina Fernández de Kirchner</a> considered him a political rival. Following the <a href="/wiki/Resignation_of_Pope_Benedict_XVI" title="Resignation of Pope Benedict XVI">resignation of Pope Benedict XVI</a> on 28 February 2013, <a href="/wiki/Papal_conclave,_2013" title="Papal conclave, 2013">a papal conclave</a> elected Bergoglio as his successor on 13 March.</p>
<p>Throughout his public life, Pope Francis has been noted for his humility, emphasis on God's mercy, concern for the <a href="/wiki/Poverty" title="Poverty">poor</a>, populist causes and commitment to <a href="/wiki/Interfaith_dialogue" title="Interfaith dialogue">interfaith dialogue</a>. He is credited with having a less formal approach to the papacy than his predecessors, for instance choosing to reside in the <i><a href="/wiki/Domus_Sanctae_Marthae" title="Domus Sanctae Marthae">Domus Sanctae Marthae</a></i> guesthouse rather than in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papal_apartments" title="Papal apartments">papal apartments</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Palace" title="Apostolic Palace">Apostolic Palace</a> used by his predecessors. In addition, due to both his Jesuit and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ignatian" title="Ignatian">Ignatian</a> aesthetic, he is known for favoring simpler <a href="/wiki/Vestment" title="Vestment">vestments</a> void of ornamentation, including refusing the traditional <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papal_mozzetta" title="Papal mozzetta">papal mozzetta</a> cape upon his election, choosing silver instead of gold for his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Piscatory_ring" title="Piscatory ring">piscatory ring</a>, and keeping the same <a href="/wiki/Pectoral_cross" title="Pectoral cross">pectoral cross</a> he had as cardinal. He maintains that the church should be more open and welcoming. He does not support unbridled <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">capitalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marxism" title="Marxism">Marxism</a>, or Marxist versions of <a href="/wiki/Liberation_theology" title="Liberation theology">liberation theology</a>. Francis maintains the traditional views of the church regarding abortion, euthanasia, contraception, homosexuality, ordination of women, and priestly celibacy. He opposes <a href="/wiki/Consumerism" title="Consumerism">consumerism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Overdevelopment" title="Overdevelopment">irresponsible development</a>, and supports taking action on <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, a focus of his papacy with the promulgation of <i><a href="/wiki/Laudato_si%27" title="Laudato si'">Laudato si'</a></i>. In international diplomacy, he helped to restore <a href="/wiki/United_States%E2%80%93Cuban_Thaw" title="United States–Cuban Thaw">full diplomatic relations between the U.S. and Cuba</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jorge_Mario_Bergoglio_attended_a_salesian_school_between_1948_and_1949.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="657" data-file-width="960" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Jorge_Mario_Bergoglio_attended_a_salesian_school_between_1948_and_1949.jpg/220px-Jorge_Mario_Bergoglio_attended_a_salesian_school_between_1948_and_1949.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Jorge_Mario_Bergoglio_attended_a_salesian_school_between_1948_and_1949.jpg/330px-Jorge_Mario_Bergoglio_attended_a_salesian_school_between_1948_and_1949.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Jorge_Mario_Bergoglio_attended_a_salesian_school_between_1948_and_1949.jpg/440px-Jorge_Mario_Bergoglio_attended_a_salesian_school_between_1948_and_1949.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jorge_Mario_Bergoglio_attended_a_salesian_school_between_1948_and_1949.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Jorge Mario Bergoglio (fourth boy from the left on the third row from the top) at age 12, while studying at the Salesian College.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Jorge Mario Bergoglio was born on 17 December 1936<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-directory_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-directory-5">[3]</a></sup> in <a href="/wiki/Flores,_Buenos_Aires" title="Flores, Buenos Aires">Flores</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Remeseira_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Remeseira-6">[4]</a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Buenos_Aires" title="Subdivisions of Buenos Aires">neighborhood</a> of <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-directory_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-directory-5">[3]</a></sup> He was the eldest<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Garrido_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Garrido-7">[5]</a></sup> of five children of Mario José Bergoglio (1908–1959) and Regina María Sívori (1911–1981). Mario Bergoglio was an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_Argentine" title="Italian Argentine">Italian immigrant</a> accountant<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-biografia_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-biografia-8">[6]</a></sup> born in <a href="/wiki/Portacomaro" title="Portacomaro">Portacomaro</a> (<a href="/wiki/Province_of_Asti" title="Province of Asti">Province of Asti</a>) in Italy's <a href="/wiki/Piedmont" title="Piedmont">Piedmont</a> region. Regina Sívori<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sivori_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sivori-9">[7]</a></sup> was a housewife born in Buenos Aires to a family of <a href="/wiki/Northern_Italy" title="Northern Italy">northern Italian</a> (Piedmontese-Genoese) origin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guardian_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-10">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Donovan_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Donovan-11">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Henderson_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Henderson-12">[10]</a></sup> Mario José's family left Italy in 1929, to escape the fascist rule of <a href="/wiki/Benito_Mussolini" title="Benito Mussolini">Benito Mussolini</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERosalesOlivera20135_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERosalesOlivera20135-13">[11]</a></sup> María Elena Bergoglio, the Pope's only living sibling, confirmed that their emigration was not for economic reasons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fascism_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-fascism-14">[12]</a></sup> His other siblings were Alberto Horacio, Oscar Adrián and Marta Regina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[13]</a></sup> Two great-nephews, Antonio and Joseph, died in a traffic collision.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tribune_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tribune-16">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nephews_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-nephews-17">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the sixth grade, Bergoglio attended Wilfrid Barón de los Santos Ángeles, a school of the <a href="/wiki/Salesians_of_Don_Bosco" title="Salesians of Don Bosco">Salesians of Don Bosco</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Ramos_Mej%C3%ADa" title="Ramos Mejía">Ramos Mejía</a>, Buenos Aires. He attended the technical secondary school Escuela Técnica Industrial N° 27 Hipólito Yrigoyen,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-techniciandegree_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-techniciandegree-18">[16]</a></sup> named after <a href="/wiki/Hip%C3%B3lito_Yrigoyen" title="Hipólito Yrigoyen">a past President of Argentina</a>, and graduated with a chemical technician's diploma.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-directory_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-directory-5">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bio_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-bio-19">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[18]</a></sup> He worked for a few years in that capacity in the foods section at Hickethier-Bachmann Laboratory<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clarin_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Clarin-21">[19]</a></sup> where his boss was <a href="/wiki/Esther_Ballestrino" title="Esther Ballestrino">Esther Ballestrino</a>. Before joining the Jesuits, Bergoglio worked as a bar bouncer and as a janitor sweeping floors, and he also ran tests in a chemical laboratory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-burke_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-burke-22">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chua_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chua-23">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the only known health crisis of his youth, at the age of 21 he suffered from life-threatening pneumonia and three cysts. He had part of a lung excised shortly afterwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-techniciandegree_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-techniciandegree-18">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-reuters_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-24">[22]</a></sup> Bergoglio has been a lifelong supporter of <a href="/wiki/San_Lorenzo_de_Almagro" title="San Lorenzo de Almagro">San Lorenzo de Almagro</a> <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> club.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lorenzo_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lorenzo-25">[23]</a></sup> Bergoglio is also a fan of the films of <a href="/wiki/Tita_Merello" title="Tita Merello">Tita Merello</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aicabio_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-aicabio-26">[24]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Neorealism_(art)#Films" title="Neorealism (art)">neorealism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tango" title="Tango">tango</a> dancing, with an "intense fondness" for the traditional music of Argentina and <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">Uruguay</a> known as the <i><a href="/wiki/Milonga_(music)" title="Milonga (music)">milonga</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aicabio_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-aicabio-26">[24]</a></sup></p>

<th scope="row"><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Angelo_de_Donatis&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Angelo de Donatis (page does not exist)">Angelo de Donatis</a></th>
<td>9 November 2015</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Peter_Bryan_Wells" title="Peter Bryan Wells">Peter Bryan Wells</a></th>
<td>19 March 2016</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Miguel_%C3%81ngel_Ayuso_Guixot" title="Miguel Ángel Ayuso Guixot">Miguel Ángel Ayuso Guixot</a></th>
<td>19 March 2016</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Bergoglio found his vocation to the priesthood while he was on his way to celebrate the <a href="/wiki/Spring_Day#Argentina" title="Spring Day">Spring Day</a>. He passed by a church to go to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sacrament_of_Penance_%26_Reconciliation_(Catholic_Church)" title="Sacrament of Penance &amp; Reconciliation (Catholic Church)">confession</a>, and was inspired by the priest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[26]</a></sup> Bergoglio studied at the archdiocesan <a href="/wiki/Seminary" title="Seminary">seminary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Inmaculada_Concepci%C3%B3n_Seminary" title="Inmaculada Concepción Seminary">Inmaculada Concepción Seminary</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Villa_Devoto" title="Villa Devoto">Villa Devoto</a>, Buenos Aires, and, after three years, entered the Society of Jesus as a novice on 11 March 1958.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aicabio_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-aicabio-26">[24]</a></sup> Bergoglio has said that, as a young seminarian, he had a crush on a girl he met and briefly doubted about continuing the religious career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celibacy_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-celibacy-29">[27]</a></sup> As a Jesuit novice he studied humanities in <a href="/wiki/Santiago" title="Santiago">Santiago</a>, Chile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[28]</a></sup> At the conclusion of his novitiate in the Society of Jesus, Bergoglio officially became a Jesuit on 12 March 1960, when he made the religious profession of the initial, perpetual vows of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Poverty,_chastity_and_obedience" title="Poverty, chastity and obedience">poverty, chastity and obedience</a> of a member of the order.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RO42_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-RO42-32">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1960, Bergoglio obtained a <a href="/wiki/Licentiate#Argentina" title="Licentiate">licentiate</a> in philosophy from the <a href="/wiki/Colegio_M%C3%A1ximo_de_San_Jos%C3%A9" title="Colegio Máximo de San José">Colegio Máximo de San José</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Miguel,_Buenos_Aires" title="San Miguel, Buenos Aires">San Miguel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires_Province" title="Buenos Aires Province">Buenos Aires Province</a>. He taught literature and <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">psychology</a> at the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Colegio_de_la_Inmaculada_Concepci%C3%B3n_(Argentina)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Colegio de la Inmaculada Concepción (Argentina) (page does not exist)">Colegio de la Inmaculada Concepción</a>, a high school in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe,_Argentina" title="Santa Fe, Argentina">Santa Fe</a>, from 1964 to 1965. In 1966 he taught the same courses at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colegio_del_Salvador_(Argentina)" title="Colegio del Salvador (Argentina)">Colegio del Salvador</a> in Buenos Aires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-directory_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-directory-5">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[31]</a></sup> In 1967, Bergoglio finished his theological studies and was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holy_Orders" title="Holy Orders">ordained</a> to the priesthood on 13 December 1969, by Archbishop <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Jos%C3%A9_Castellano" title="Ramón José Castellano">Ramón José Castellano</a>. He attended the <a href="/wiki/Facultades_de_Filosof%C3%ADa_y_Teolog%C3%ADa_de_San_Miguel" title="Facultades de Filosofía y Teología de San Miguel">Facultades de Filosofía y Teología de San Miguel</a> (Philosophical and Theological Faculty of San Miguel), a seminary in San Miguel. He served as the <a href="/wiki/Master_of_novices" title="Master of novices">master of novices</a> for the province there and became a professor of theology.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bergoglio completed his final stage of spiritual training as a Jesuit, <a href="/wiki/Tertianship" title="Tertianship">tertianship</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Alcal%C3%A1_de_Henares" title="Alcalá de Henares">Alcalá de Henares</a>, Spain. He took the final <a href="/wiki/Fourth_vow" title="Fourth vow">fourth vow</a> (obedience to the pope) in the Society of Jesus on 22 April 1973.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RO42_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-RO42-32">[30]</a></sup> He was named <a href="/wiki/Provincial_superior" title="Provincial superior">provincial superior</a> of the Society of Jesus in Argentina on 31 July 1973 and served until 1979.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-directory_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-directory-5">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sjvows_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-sjvows-35">[33]</a></sup> He made a pilgrimage to Jerusalem in 1973, shortly after being named provincial superior, but his stay was shortened by the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War" title="Yom Kippur War">Yom Kippur War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-travel_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-travel-36">[34]</a></sup> After the completion of his term of office, in 1980 he was named the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rector_(academic)" title="Rector (academic)">rector</a> of the Philosophical and Theological Faculty of San Miguel in San Miguel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[35]</a></sup> Before taking up this new appointment, he spent the first three months of 1980 in Ireland to learn English, staying at the Jesuit Centre at the <a href="/wiki/Milltown_Institute_of_Theology_and_Philosophy" title="Milltown Institute of Theology and Philosophy">Milltown Institute of Theology and Philosophy</a>, Dublin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[36]</a></sup> After returning to Argentina to take up his new post at San Miguel, Father Bergoglio served in that capacity until 1986.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-directory_5-5"><a href="#cite_note-directory-5">[3]</a></sup> He was removed as rector by the Jesuit superior-general <a href="/wiki/Peter_Hans_Kolvenbach" title="Peter Hans Kolvenbach">Peter Hans Kolvenbach</a> because Bergoglio's policy of educating the young Jesuits in direct pastoral work and in popular religiosity was opposed to the worldwide trend in the Society of Jesus of emphasizing social justice based on sociological analysis, especially promoted by the Centro de Investigaciones y Accion Social (CIAS).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-39">[37]</a></sup></p>
<p>He spent several months at the <a href="/wiki/Sankt_Georgen_Graduate_School_of_Philosophy_and_Theology" title="Sankt Georgen Graduate School of Philosophy and Theology">Sankt Georgen Graduate School of Philosophy and Theology</a> in Frankfurt, Germany, while considering possible <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dissertation" title="Dissertation">dissertation</a> topics,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[38]</a></sup> before returning to Argentina to serve as a <a href="/wiki/Confessor" title="Confessor">confessor</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spiritual_director" title="Spiritual director">spiritual director</a> to the Jesuit community in <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Argentina" title="Córdoba, Argentina">Córdoba</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-litoral_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-litoral-41">[39]</a></sup> In Germany, he saw the painting <i><a href="/wiki/Mary_Untier_of_Knots" title="Mary Untier of Knots">Mary Untier of Knots</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Augsburg" title="Augsburg">Augsburg</a> and brought a copy of the painting to Argentina where it has become an important <a href="/wiki/Marian_devotions" title="Marian devotions">Marian devotion</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[c]</a></sup> As a student at the Salesian school, Bergoglio was mentored by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ukrainian_Greek_Catholic" title="Ukrainian Greek Catholic">Ukrainian Greek Catholic</a> priest <a href="/wiki/Stefan_Czmil" title="Stefan Czmil">Stefan Czmil</a>. Bergoglio often rose hours before his classmates to serve Mass for Czmil.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greek_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-greek-47">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>Because of continued tensions with Jesuit leaders and scholars, a sense of Bergoglio's "dissent", views of his orthodoxy and opposition to theology of liberation, and his work as auxiliary bishop of Buenos Aires, he was asked in 1992 by Jesuit authorities not to reside in Jesuit houses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncronline.org_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-ncronline.org-48">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[48]</a></sup> From then on, he did not visit Jesuit houses and was in "virtual estrangement from the Jesuits" until after his election as Pope.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_39-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-39">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ncronline.org_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-ncronline.org-48">[45]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bishop_.281992.E2.80.932001.29">Bishop (1992–2001)</span></h3>
<p>Bergoglio was named Auxiliary Bishop of Buenos Aires in 1992 and <a href="/wiki/Consecration#Ordination_of_bishops" title="Consecration">ordained</a> on 27 June 1992 as <a href="/wiki/Auca_(titular_diocese)" title="Auca (titular diocese)">Titular Bishop of Auca</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-directory_5-6"><a href="#cite_note-directory-5">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[49]</a></sup> with Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Quarracino" title="Antonio Quarracino">Antonio Quarracino</a>, Archbishop of Buenos Aires, serving as principal consecrator.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aica_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-aica-27">[25]</a></sup> He chose as his episcopal motto <i>Miserando atque eligendo</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[50]</a></sup> It is drawn from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Bede" title="Saint Bede">Saint Bede</a>'s homily on Matthew 9:9–13: "because he saw him through the eyes of mercy and chose him".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Catholic_News_Service_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Catholic_News_Service-54">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 3 June 1997, Bergoglio was appointed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coadjutor_Bishop" title="Coadjutor Bishop">Coadjutor Archbishop</a> of Buenos Aires with right of automatic succession. Upon Quarracino's death on 28 February 1998, Bergoglio became Metropolitan Archbishop of Buenos Aires. In that role, Bergoglio created new parishes and restructured the archdiocese administrative offices, led pro-life initiatives, and created a commission on divorces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-directory_5-7"><a href="#cite_note-directory-5">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[52]</a></sup> One of Bergoglio's major initiatives as archbishop was to increase the Church's presence in the slums of Buenos Aires. Under his leadership, the number of priests assigned to work in the slums doubled.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[53]</a></sup> This work led to him being called the "Slum Bishop".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>Early in his time as Archbishop of Buenos Aires, Bergoglio sold off the archdiocese's shares in multiple banks and turned its accounts into those of a normal customer in international banks. The shares in banks had led the local church to a high leniency towards high spending, and the archdiocese was nearing bankruptcy as a result. As a normal customer of the bank, the church was forced into a higher fiscal discipline.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 6 November 1998, while remaining Archbishop of Buenos Aires, he was named <a href="/wiki/Ordinary_(officer)" title="Ordinary (officer)">ordinary</a> for those <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Rite_Catholic_Churches" title="Eastern Rite Catholic Churches">Eastern Catholics</a> in Argentina who lacked a <a href="/wiki/Prelate" title="Prelate">prelate</a> of their own rite.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aica_27-2"><a href="#cite_note-aica-27">[25]</a></sup> Major Archbishop <a href="/wiki/Sviatoslav_Shevchuk" title="Sviatoslav Shevchuk">Sviatoslav Shevchuk</a> has said that Bergoglio understands the liturgy, rites, and spirituality of his Greek Catholic Church and always "took care of our Church in Argentina" as ordinary for Eastern Catholics during his time as Archbishop of Buenos Aires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greek_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-greek-47">[44]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2000, Bergoglio was the only church official to reconcile with <a href="/wiki/Jer%C3%B3nimo_Podest%C3%A1" title="Jerónimo Podestá">Jerónimo Podestá</a>, a former bishop who had been suspended as a priest after opposing the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Revolution" title="Argentine Revolution">Argentine Revolution</a> military dictatorship in 1972. He defended Podestá's wife from Vatican attacks on their marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[56]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[58]</a></sup> That same year, Bergoglio said the Argentine Catholic Church needed "to put on garments of public penance for the sins committed during the years of the dictatorship" in the 1970s, during the <a href="/wiki/Dirty_War" title="Dirty War">Dirty War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bergoglio made it his custom to celebrate the <a href="/wiki/Maundy_Thursday" title="Maundy Thursday">Holy Thursday</a> ritual <a href="/wiki/Foot_washing#Roman_Catholic_practice" title="Foot washing">washing of feet</a> in places such as jails, hospitals, retirement homes or slums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[60]</a></sup> In 2007, just two days after Benedict XVI issued <a href="/wiki/Summorum_Pontificum" title="Summorum Pontificum">new rules</a> for using the liturgical forms that preceded the <a href="/wiki/Second_Vatican_Council" title="Second Vatican Council">Second Vatican Council</a>, Cardinal Bergoglio was one of the first bishops in the world to respond by instituting a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tridentine_liturgy" title="Tridentine liturgy">Tridentine Mass</a> in Buenos Aires.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[61]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[62]</a></sup> It was celebrated weekly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 8 November 2005, Bergoglio was elected president of the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Episcopal_Conference" title="Argentine Episcopal Conference">Argentine Episcopal Conference</a> for a three-year term (2005–08).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[64]</a></sup> He was reelected to another three-year term on 11 November 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[65]</a></sup> He remained a member of that commission's permanent governing body, president of its committee for the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Catholic_University_of_Argentina" title="Pontifical Catholic University of Argentina">Pontifical Catholic University of Argentina</a>, and a member of its liturgy committee for the care of shrines.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aica_27-3"><a href="#cite_note-aica-27">[25]</a></sup> While head of the Argentine Catholic bishops' conference, Bergoglio issued a collective apology for his church's failure to protect people from the Junta during the Dirty War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[66]</a></sup> When he turned 75 in December 2011, Bergoglio submitted his resignation as Archbishop of Buenos Aires to Pope Benedict XVI as required by <a href="/wiki/Canon_law_(Catholic_Church)" title="Canon law (Catholic Church)">canon law</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-travel_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-travel-36">[34]</a></sup> Still, as he had no coadjutor archbishop, he stayed in office, waiting for an eventual replacement appointed by the Vatican.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cardinal_.282001.E2.80.932013.29">Cardinal (2001–2013)</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cat%C3%A9ch%C3%A8se_18_juin_2008_par_le_cardinal_Bergoglio_-2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1824" data-file-width="1216" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Cat%C3%A9ch%C3%A8se_18_juin_2008_par_le_cardinal_Bergoglio_-2.jpg/150px-Cat%C3%A9ch%C3%A8se_18_juin_2008_par_le_cardinal_Bergoglio_-2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Cat%C3%A9ch%C3%A8se_18_juin_2008_par_le_cardinal_Bergoglio_-2.jpg/225px-Cat%C3%A9ch%C3%A8se_18_juin_2008_par_le_cardinal_Bergoglio_-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Cat%C3%A9ch%C3%A8se_18_juin_2008_par_le_cardinal_Bergoglio_-2.jpg/300px-Cat%C3%A9ch%C3%A8se_18_juin_2008_par_le_cardinal_Bergoglio_-2.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cat%C3%A9ch%C3%A8se_18_juin_2008_par_le_cardinal_Bergoglio_-2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bergoglio on 18 June 2008 giving a catechesis</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the <a href="/wiki/Papal_consistory" title="Papal consistory">consistory</a> of 21 February 2001, Archbishop Bergoglio was created a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardinal_(Catholicism)" title="Cardinal (Catholicism)">cardinal</a> by <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Titular_church" title="Titular church">title</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardinal_priest" title="Cardinal priest">cardinal-priest</a> of <a href="/wiki/San_Roberto_Bellarmino_(church)" title="San Roberto Bellarmino (church)">San Roberto Bellarmino</a>, a church served by Jesuits and named for one; he was formally installed in that church the following 14 October. When he traveled to Rome for the ceremony, he and his sister María Elena visited the village in northern Italy where their father was born.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fascism_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-fascism-14">[12]</a></sup> As cardinal, Bergoglio was appointed to five administrative positions in the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Curia" title="Roman Curia">Roman Curia</a>. He was a member of the <a href="/wiki/Congregation_for_Divine_Worship_and_the_Discipline_of_the_Sacraments" title="Congregation for Divine Worship and the Discipline of the Sacraments">Congregation for Divine Worship and the Discipline of the Sacraments</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Congregation_for_the_Clergy" title="Congregation for the Clergy">Congregation for the Clergy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Congregation_for_Institutes_of_Consecrated_Life_and_Societies_of_Apostolic_Life" title="Congregation for Institutes of Consecrated Life and Societies of Apostolic Life">Congregation for Institutes of Consecrated Life and Societies of Apostolic Life</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Council_for_the_Family" title="Pontifical Council for the Family">Pontifical Council for the Family</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Commission_for_Latin_America" title="Pontifical Commission for Latin America">Commission for Latin America</a>. Later that year, when Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Edward_Egan" title="Edward Egan">Edward Egan</a> returned to New York following the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">September 11 attacks</a>, Bergoglio replaced him as relator (recording secretary) in the <a href="/wiki/Synod_of_Bishops_(Catholic)" title="Synod of Bishops (Catholic)">Synod of Bishops</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[68]</a></sup> and, according to the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic_Herald" title="Catholic Herald">Catholic Herald</a></i>, created "a favourable impression as a man open to communion and dialogue".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thunder_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-thunder-72">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[70]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Card._Jorge_Bergoglio_SJ,_2008.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1177" data-file-width="991" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Card._Jorge_Bergoglio_SJ%2C_2008.jpg/170px-Card._Jorge_Bergoglio_SJ%2C_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Card._Jorge_Bergoglio_SJ%2C_2008.jpg/255px-Card._Jorge_Bergoglio_SJ%2C_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Card._Jorge_Bergoglio_SJ%2C_2008.jpg/340px-Card._Jorge_Bergoglio_SJ%2C_2008.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Card._Jorge_Bergoglio_SJ,_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Cardinal Jorge Bergoglio in 2008</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cardinal Bergoglio became known for personal humility, doctrinal conservatism, and a commitment to <a href="/wiki/Social_justice" title="Social justice">social justice</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allen_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-Allen-74">[71]</a></sup> A <a href="/wiki/Simple_living" title="Simple living">simple lifestyle</a> contributed to his reputation for humility. He lived in a small apartment, rather than in the elegant bishop's residence in the suburb of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Olivos,_Buenos_Aires_Province" title="Olivos, Buenos Aires Province">Olivos</a>. He took public transportation and cooked his own meals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[72]</a></sup> He limited his time in Rome to "lightning visits".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-falasca_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-falasca-76">[73]</a></sup> He was known to be devoted to <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9r%C3%A8se_of_Lisieux" title="Thérèse of Lisieux">St. Therese of Lisieux</a>, and he enclosed a small picture of her in the letters he wrote, calling her "a great missionary saint".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[74]</a></sup></p>
<p>After Pope John Paul II died on 2 April 2005, Bergoglio attended his <a href="/wiki/Funeral_of_Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Funeral of Pope John Paul II">funeral</a> and was considered one of the <i><a href="/wiki/Papabile" title="Papabile">papabile</a></i> for succession to the papacy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[75]</a></sup> He participated as a <a href="/wiki/Cardinal_electors_for_the_papal_conclave,_2005" title="Cardinal electors for the papal conclave, 2005">cardinal elector</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Papal_conclave,_2005" title="Papal conclave, 2005">2005 papal conclave</a> that elected Pope Benedict XVI. In the <i><a href="/wiki/National_Catholic_Reporter" title="National Catholic Reporter">National Catholic Reporter</a></i>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_L._Allen,_Jr." title="John L. Allen, Jr.">John L. Allen, Jr.</a> reported that Bergoglio was a frontrunner in the 2005 conclave.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allen_74-1"><a href="#cite_note-Allen-74">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[76]</a></sup> In September 2005, the Italian magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Limes_(magazine)" title="Limes (magazine)">Limes</a></i> published claims that Bergoglio had been the runner-up and main challenger to Cardinal Ratzinger at that conclave and that he had received 40 votes in the third ballot, but fell back to 26 at the fourth and decisive ballot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN05_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN05-80">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-votes2005_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-votes2005-81">[78]</a></sup> The claims were based on a diary purportedly belonging to an anonymous cardinal who had been present at the conclave.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN05_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-CNN05-80">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rubin13_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rubin13-82">[79]</a></sup> According to the Italian journalist <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Andrea_Tornielli&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Andrea Tornielli (page does not exist)">Andrea Tornielli</a>, this number of votes had no precedent for a Latin American <i>papabile</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rubin13_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rubin13-82">[79]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/La_Stampa" title="La Stampa">La Stampa</a></i> reported that Bergoglio was in close contention with Ratzinger during the election, until he made an emotional plea that the cardinals should not vote for him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tears_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-tears-83">[80]</a></sup> According to Tornielli, Bergoglio made this request to prevent the conclave from delaying too much in the election of a pope.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a cardinal, Bergoglio was associated with <a href="/wiki/Communion_and_Liberation" title="Communion and Liberation">Communion and Liberation</a>, a Catholic evangelical lay movement of the type known as <a href="/wiki/Associations_of_the_faithful" title="Associations of the faithful">associations of the faithful</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allen_74-2"><a href="#cite_note-Allen-74">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[82]</a></sup> He sometimes made appearances at the annual gathering known as the <a href="/wiki/Meeting_for_friendship_among_peoples" title="Meeting for friendship among peoples">Rimini Meeting</a> held during the late summer months in Italy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allen_74-3"><a href="#cite_note-Allen-74">[71]</a></sup> In 2005, Cardinal Bergoglio authorized the request for <a href="/wiki/Beatification" title="Beatification">beatification</a>—the third step towards <a href="/wiki/Saint" title="Saint">sainthood</a>—for six members of the <a href="/wiki/Pallottines" title="Pallottines">Pallottine</a> community murdered in the <a href="/wiki/San_Patricio_Church_massacre" title="San Patricio Church massacre">San Patricio Church massacre</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CT2005_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-CT2005-87">[84]</a></sup> At the same time, Bergoglio ordered an investigation into the murders themselves, which had been widely blamed on the <a href="/wiki/National_Reorganization_Process" title="National Reorganization Process">National Reorganization Process</a>, the military junta that ruled Argentina at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CT2005_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-CT2005-87">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Relations_with_Argentine_governments">Relations with Argentine governments</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dirty_War">Dirty War</span></h3>
<p>Bergoglio was the subject of allegations regarding the kidnapping of two <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Jesuit</a> priests during Argentina's <a href="/wiki/Dirty_War" title="Dirty War">Dirty War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes1_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-88">[85]</a></sup> He feared for the priests' safety and had tried to change their work prior to their arrest; however, contrary to reports, he never tried to throw them out of the Jesuit order.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[86]</a></sup> In 2005, <a href="/wiki/Myriam_Bregman" title="Myriam Bregman">Myriam Bregman</a>, a human rights lawyer, filed a criminal complaint against Bergoglio, as superior in the Society of Jesus of Argentina, accusing him of involvement in the Navy's kidnapping of the two priests in May 1976.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes1_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-latimes1-90">[87]</a></sup> The lawyer's complaint did not specify the nature of Bergoglio's alleged involvement, and Bergoglio's spokesman flatly denied the allegations. The lawsuit was ultimately dismissed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nytimes1_88-1"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-88">[85]</a></sup> The priests, Orlando Yorio and <a href="/wiki/Franz_Jalics" title="Franz Jalics">Franz Jalics</a>, had been tortured,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rubin_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-rubin-91">[88]</a></sup> but found alive five months later, drugged and semi-naked. Yorio accused Bergoglio of effectively handing them over to the death squads by declining to tell the authorities that he endorsed their work. Yorio, who died in 2000, said in a 1999 interview that he believed that Bergoglio did nothing "to free us, in fact just the opposite".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WAPO_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-WAPO-92">[89]</a></sup> Jalics initially refused to discuss the complaint after moving into seclusion in a German monastery.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[90]</a></sup> However, two days after the election of Pope Francis, Jalics issued a statement confirming the kidnapping and attributing the cause to a former lay colleague who became a guerrilla, was captured, and named Yorio and Jalics when interrogated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[91]</a></sup> The following week, Jalics issued a second, clarifying statement: "It is wrong to assert that our capture took place at the initiative of Father Bergoglio … the fact is, Orlando Yorio and I were not denounced by Father Bergoglio."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[92]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bergoglio told his authorized biographer, <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Rubin" title="Sergio Rubin">Sergio Rubin</a>, that after the priests' imprisonment, he worked behind the scenes for their release; Bergoglio's intercession with dictator <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Rafael_Videla" title="Jorge Rafael Videla">Jorge Rafael Videla</a> on their behalf may have saved their lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[94]</a></sup> Bergoglio also told Rubin that he had often sheltered people from the dictatorship on church property, and once gave his own identity papers to a man who looked like him, so he could flee Argentina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rubin_91-1"><a href="#cite_note-rubin-91">[88]</a></sup> The interview with Rubin, reflected in the biography <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_jesuita" title="El jesuita">El jesuita</a></i>, is the only time Bergoglio has spoken to the press about those events.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[95]</a></sup> Alicia Oliveira, a former Argentine judge, has also reported that Bergoglio helped people flee Argentina during the rule of the junta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[96]</a></sup> Since Francis became Pope, Gonzalo Mosca<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[97]</a></sup> and José Caravias<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[98]</a></sup> have related to journalists accounts of how Bergoglio helped them flee the Argentine dictatorship.</p>
<p>Oliveira described the future Pope as "anguished" and "very critical of the dictatorship" during the Dirty War.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[99]</a></sup> Oliveira met with him at the time and urged Bergoglio to speak out—he told her that "he couldn't. That it wasn't an easy thing to do."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WAPO_92-1"><a href="#cite_note-WAPO-92">[89]</a></sup> Artist and human rights activist <a href="/wiki/Adolfo_P%C3%A9rez_Esquivel" title="Adolfo Pérez Esquivel">Adolfo Pérez Esquivel</a>, the 1980 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> laureate, said: "Perhaps he didn't have the courage of other priests, but he never collaborated with the dictatorship … Bergoglio was no accomplice of the dictatorship."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[101]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Graciela_Fern%C3%A1ndez_Meijide" title="Graciela Fernández Meijide">Graciela Fernández Meijide</a>, member of the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Assembly_for_Human_Rights" title="Permanent Assembly for Human Rights">Permanent Assembly for Human Rights</a>, also said that there was no proof linking Bergoglio with the dictatorship. She told to the <i><a href="/wiki/Clar%C3%ADn_(Argentine_newspaper)" title="Clarín (Argentine newspaper)">Clarín</a></i> newspaper: "There is no information and Justice couldn't prove it. I was in the <a href="/wiki/Permanent_Assembly_for_Human_Rights" title="Permanent Assembly for Human Rights">APDH</a> during all the dictatorship years and I received hundreds of testimonies. Bergoglio was never mentioned. It was the same in the <a href="/wiki/National_Commission_on_the_Disappearance_of_Persons" title="National Commission on the Disappearance of Persons">CONADEP</a>. Nobody mentioned him as instigator or as anything."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[102]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ricardo_Lorenzetti" title="Ricardo Lorenzetti">Ricardo Lorenzetti</a>, President of the Argentine Supreme Court, also has said that Bergoglio is "completely innocent" of the accusations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[103]</a></sup> Historian <a href="/wiki/Uki_Go%C3%B1i" title="Uki Goñi">Uki Goñi</a> pointed that, during the early 1976, the military junta still had a good image among society, and that the scale of the political repression was not known until much later; Bergoglio would have had little reason to suspect that the detention of Yorio and Jalics could end up in their deaths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[104]</a></sup></p>
<p>When Bergoglio became Pope, an alleged photo of him giving the <a href="/wiki/Sacramental_bread" title="Sacramental bread">sacramental bread</a> to dictator Jorge Rafael Videla became viral in social networks. It has also been used by the newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/P%C3%A1gina/12" title="Página/12">Página/12</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[105]</a></sup> The photo was soon proved to be false. It was revealed that the priest, whose face is not visible in the photo, was Carlos Berón de Astrada. The photo was taken at the church "Pequeña Obra de la Divina Providencia Don Orione" in 1990, not during the Dirty War, and after Videla's presidential pardon. The photo was produced by the agency AFP and it was initially published by the <i><a href="/wiki/Cr%C3%B3nica_(newspaper)" title="Crónica (newspaper)">Crónica</a></i> newspaper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[106]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fernando_de_la_R.C3.BAa">Fernando de la Rúa</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Fernando_de_la_R%C3%BAa" title="Fernando de la Rúa">Fernando de la Rúa</a> replaced <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Menem" title="Carlos Menem">Carlos Menem</a> as president of Argentina in 1999. As an archbishop, Bergoglio celebrated the annual Mass at the <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires_Metropolitan_Cathedral" title="Buenos Aires Metropolitan Cathedral">Buenos Aires Metropolitan Cathedral</a> on the <i><a href="/wiki/First_National_Government" title="First National Government">First National Government</a></i> holiday, 25 May. In 2000, Bergoglio criticized the perceived apathy of society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[107]</a></sup> Argentina faced an <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%932002_Argentine_great_depression" title="1998–2002 Argentine great depression">economic depression</a> at the time, and the Church criticized the fiscal austerity of the government, which increased poverty. De la Rúa asked the Church to promote a dialogue between the leaders of economic and political sectors to find a solution for the crisis. He claims that he talked with Bergoglio and proposed to take part in the meeting, but Bergoglio would have told him that the meeting was cancelled because of a misunderstanding by De la Rúa's assistant, who may have declined the president's assistance. Bishop <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jorge_Casaretto&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jorge Casaretto (page does not exist)">Jorge Casaretto</a> considers it unlikely, as De la Rúa only made the request in newspaper interviews, but never made a formal request to the Church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[108]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Justicialist_Party" title="Justicialist Party">Justicialist Party</a> won the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_legislative_election,_2001" title="Argentine legislative election, 2001">2001 elections</a> and got the majority in the Congress, and appointed <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Puerta" title="Ramón Puerta">Ramón Puerta</a> as president of the Senate. As vice president <a href="/wiki/Carlos_%C3%81lvarez_(politician)" title="Carlos Álvarez (politician)">Carlos Álvarez</a> resigned shortly before, this left an opposing party second in the <a href="/wiki/Argentine_order_of_precedence" title="Argentine order of precedence">order of precedence</a>. Bergoglio asked for an interview with Puerta, and had a positive impression of him. Puerta told him that the Justicialist party was not plotting to oust De la Rúa, and promised to help the president promote the laws that may be required.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[109]</a></sup></p>
<p>During police repression of the <a href="/wiki/December_2001_riots_in_Argentina" title="December 2001 riots in Argentina">riots of December 2001</a>, he contacted the Ministry of the Interior and asked that the police distinguish rioters engaged in acts of vandalism from peaceful protesters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[110]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nestor_and_Cristina_Kirchner">Nestor and Cristina Kirchner</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pope_Francis_with_Cristina_Fernandez_de_Kirchner_4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1342" data-file-width="2000" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Pope_Francis_with_Cristina_Fernandez_de_Kirchner_4.jpg/220px-Pope_Francis_with_Cristina_Fernandez_de_Kirchner_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Pope_Francis_with_Cristina_Fernandez_de_Kirchner_4.jpg/330px-Pope_Francis_with_Cristina_Fernandez_de_Kirchner_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Pope_Francis_with_Cristina_Fernandez_de_Kirchner_4.jpg/440px-Pope_Francis_with_Cristina_Fernandez_de_Kirchner_4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pope_Francis_with_Cristina_Fernandez_de_Kirchner_4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pope Francis with Argentine president <a href="/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Kirchner" title="Cristina Fernández de Kirchner">Cristina Fernández de Kirchner</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>When Bergoglio celebrated Mass at the Cathedral for the 2004 <i>First National Government</i> holiday, President <a href="/wiki/N%C3%A9stor_Kirchner" title="Néstor Kirchner">Néstor Kirchner</a> attended and heard Bergoglio request more political dialogue, reject intolerance, and criticize exhibitionism and strident announcements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[111]</a></sup> Kirchner celebrated the national day elsewhere the following year and the Mass in the Cathedral was suspended.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[112]</a></sup> In 2006, Bergoglio helped the fellow Jesuit <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joaqu%C3%ADn_Pi%C3%B1a" title="Joaquín Piña">Joaquín Piña</a> to win the elections in the <a href="/wiki/Misiones_Province" title="Misiones Province">Misiones Province</a> and prevent an amendment of the local constitution that would allow indefinite re-elections. Kirchner intended to use that project to start similar amendments at other provinces, and eventually to the national constitution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[113]</a></sup> Kirchner considered Bergoglio as a political rival to the day he died in October 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anios_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-anios-117">[114]</a></sup> Bergoglio's relations with Kirchner's widow and successor, <a href="/wiki/Cristina_Fern%C3%A1ndez_de_Kirchner" title="Cristina Fernández de Kirchner">Cristina Fernández de Kirchner</a>, have been similarly tense. In 2008, Bergoglio called for national reconciliation during <a href="/wiki/2008_Argentine_government_conflict_with_the_agricultural_sector" title="2008 Argentine government conflict with the agricultural sector">disturbances</a> in the country's agricultural regions, which the government interpreted as a support for anti-government demonstrators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anios_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-anios-117">[114]</a></sup> The campaign to enact <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Argentina" title="Same-sex marriage in Argentina">same-sex marriage legislation</a> was a particularly tense period in their relations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-anios_117-2"><a href="#cite_note-anios-117">[114]</a></sup></p>
<p>When Bergoglio was elected pope, the initial reactions were mixed. Most of the Argentine society cheered it, but the pro-government newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/P%C3%A1gina/12" title="Página/12">Página/12</a></i> published renewed allegations about the Dirty War, and the president of the <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_the_Argentine_Republic" title="National Library of the Argentine Republic">National Library</a> described a global conspiracy theory. The president took more than an hour before congratulating the new Pope, and only did so in a passing reference within a routine speech. However, due to the Pope's popularity in Argentina, Cristina Kirchner made what the political analyst Claudio Fantini called a "<a href="/wiki/Copernican_Revolution_(metaphor)" title="Copernican Revolution (metaphor)">Copernican shift</a>" in her relations with him and fully embraced the Francis phenomenon.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[115]</a></sup> On the day before his inauguration as pope, Bergoglio, now Francis, had a private meeting with Kirchner. They exchanged gifts and lunched together. This was the new pope's first meeting with a head of state, and there was speculation that the two were mending their relations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[117]</a></sup> <i>Página/12</i> <a href="/wiki/Self-censorship" title="Self-censorship">removed</a> their controversial articles about Bergoglio, written by <a href="/wiki/Horacio_Verbitsky" title="Horacio Verbitsky">Horacio Verbitsky</a>, from their web page, as a result of this change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[118]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecumenism_with_other_Christians">Ecumenism with other Christians</span></h2>
<p>In a notable interview with <i><a href="/wiki/La_Stampa" title="La Stampa">La Stampa</a></i>, Pope Francis emphasized his commitment to <a href="/wiki/Ecumenism" title="Ecumenism">ecumenism</a>, stating: "For me, ecumenism is a priority. Today, we have the ecumenism of blood. In some countries they kill Christians because they <a href="/wiki/Cross_necklace" title="Cross necklace">wear a cross</a> or have a Bible, and before killing them they don't ask if they're Anglicans, Lutherans, Catholics or Orthodox. The blood is mixed."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[120]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/Week_of_Prayer_for_Christian_Unity" title="Week of Prayer for Christian Unity">Week of Prayer for Christian Unity</a>, Pope Francis addressed the attendees of the <i>John 17 Movement</i> gathering opining that "<a href="/wiki/Schism" title="Schism">Division</a> is the work of the <a href="/wiki/Devil_in_Christianity" title="Devil in Christianity">Father of Lies</a>" and that he "knows that Christians are disciples of Christ: that they are one, that they are brothers! He doesn’t care if they are Evangelicals, or Orthodox, Lutherans, Catholics or Apostolic…he doesn’t care! They are Christians. And that blood (of martyrdom) unites. Today, dear brothers and sisters, we are living an 'ecumenism of blood'. This must encourage us to do what we are doing today: to pray, to dialogue together, to shorten the distance between us, to strengthen our bonds of brotherhood."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[121]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[122]</a></sup> During the 2016 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Octave_of_Christian_Unity" title="Octave of Christian Unity">Octave of Christian Unity</a>, Pope Francis "asked forgiveness for the way Catholics had treated other Christian believers over the years, and also invited Catholics to pardon those who had persecuted them."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[123]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[124]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[125]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Eastern_Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodoxy</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pope_Franciscus_%26_Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_in_the_Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre_in_Jerusalem_(1).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Pope_Franciscus_%26_Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_in_the_Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre_in_Jerusalem_%281%29.JPG/220px-Pope_Franciscus_%26_Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_in_the_Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre_in_Jerusalem_%281%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Pope_Franciscus_%26_Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_in_the_Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre_in_Jerusalem_%281%29.JPG/330px-Pope_Franciscus_%26_Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_in_the_Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre_in_Jerusalem_%281%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Pope_Franciscus_%26_Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_in_the_Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre_in_Jerusalem_%281%29.JPG/440px-Pope_Franciscus_%26_Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_in_the_Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre_in_Jerusalem_%281%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pope_Franciscus_%26_Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_in_the_Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre_in_Jerusalem_(1).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pope Francis meeting with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_of_Constantinople" title="Patriarch Bartholomew I of Constantinople">Patriarch Bartholomew I</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Holy_Sepulchre" title="Church of the Holy Sepulchre">Church of the Holy Sepulchre</a> during his 2014 pilgrimage to the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">Holy Land</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bergoglio is recognized for his efforts "to further close the nearly 1,000-year estrangement with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Churches" title="Orthodox Churches">Orthodox Churches</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-orthodox_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-orthodox-129">[126]</a></sup> Antoni Sevruk, rector of the Russian Orthodox Church of Saint Catherine the Great Martyr in Rome, said that Bergoglio "often visited Orthodox services in the Russian Orthodox Annunciation Cathedral in Buenos Aires" and is known as an advocate on behalf of the Orthodox Church in dealing with Argentina's government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bergoglio's positive relationship with the Eastern Orthodox churches is reflected in the fact that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patriarch_Bartholomew_I_of_Constantinople" title="Patriarch Bartholomew I of Constantinople">Patriarch Bartholomew I of Constantinople</a> attended his installation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-patriarch_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-patriarch-131">[128]</a></sup> This is the first time since the <a href="/wiki/East%E2%80%93West_Schism" title="East–West Schism">Great Schism</a> of 1054 that the Orthodox <a href="/wiki/Ecumenical_Patriarch_of_Constantinople" title="Ecumenical Patriarch of Constantinople">Ecumenical Patriarch of Constantinople</a>, a position considered <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_among_equals" title="First among equals">first among equals</a> in the Eastern <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Church_organization" title="Orthodox Church organization">Orthodox Church organization</a>, has attended a papal installation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[129]</a></sup> Orthodox leaders state that Bartholomew's decision to attend the ceremony shows that the relationship between the Orthodox and Catholic Churches is a priority of his, but they also note that Francis' "well-documented work for social justice and his insistence that globalization is detrimental to the poor" may have created a "renewed opportunity" for the two Church communities to "work collectively on issues of mutual concern".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-patriarch_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-patriarch-131">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[d]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 12 February 2016, Pope Francis and <a href="/wiki/Patriarch_Kirill_of_Moscow" title="Patriarch Kirill of Moscow">Patriarch Kirill of Moscow</a>, head of the largest Eastern Orthodox church, met in Havana, Cuba, issuing the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Declaration_of_Pope_Francis_and_Patriarch_Kirill" title="Joint Declaration of Pope Francis and Patriarch Kirill">Joint Declaration of Pope Francis and Patriarch Kirill</a>, calling for restored Christian unity between the two churches. This was reported as the first such high-level meeting between the two churches since the <a href="/wiki/East%E2%80%93West_Schism" title="East–West Schism">Great Schism</a> of 1054.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[131]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anglicanism">Anglicanism</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Gregory_Venables" title="Gregory Venables">Gregory Venables</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglican</a> Bishop of Argentina and former Primate of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglican_Church_of_the_Southern_Cone_of_America" title="Anglican Church of the Southern Cone of America">Anglican Church of the Southern Cone of America</a>, said that Cardinal Bergoglio had told him very clearly that the <a href="/wiki/Personal_ordinariate" title="Personal ordinariate">personal ordinariates</a> established within the Catholic Church for groups of former Anglicans was "quite unnecessary" and that the Catholic Church needed Anglicans as Anglicans. A spokesman for the ordinariates said the words were those of Venables, not the Pope.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[132]</a></sup> Pope Francis met for the first time the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury" title="Archbishop of Canterbury">Archbishop of Canterbury</a>, <a href="/wiki/Justin_Welby" title="Justin Welby">Justin Welby</a>, when he visited the Vatican, on 14 June 2013. The Roman Pontiff said that they both shared the same concerns for social justice, peace and the promotion of Christian values, in matters like marriage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[133]</a></sup> The second meeting took place at the Vatican, on 16 June 2014, with Pope Francis and Justin Welby recommitting themselves to work against modern slavery and human trafficking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[134]</a></sup> Pope Francis has expressed his support for the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_realignment" title="Anglican realignment">Anglican realignment</a>, sending through his personal friend, Gregory Venables, a message to the Archbishop <a href="/wiki/Foley_Beach" title="Foley Beach">Foley Beach</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Church_in_North_America" title="Anglican Church in North America">Anglican Church in North America</a>, a newly formed church outside of the Anglican Communion and not officially recognized by the <a href="/wiki/Archbishop_of_Canterbury" title="Archbishop of Canterbury">Archbishop of Canterbury</a>, with his "personal greetings and congratulations as he leads his church in the very important job of revival" and asking Venables to embrace him on his behalf. It was presented during Archbishop Beach's enthronement, which took place at the Church of the Apostles in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, on 9 October 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</span></h3>
<p>On 31 October 2016, Pope Francis commemorated the 499th anniversary of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">Reformation</a> with Lutherans in <a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>. This event opened the 500th year<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[e]</a></sup> since the Reformation began with Martin Luther posting his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ninety-Five_Theses" title="Ninety-Five Theses">Ninety-Five Theses</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wittenberg" title="Wittenberg">Wittenberg</a> in 1517.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[136]</a></sup> The Pope visited the 950 year old <a href="/wiki/Lund_Cathedral" title="Lund Cathedral">Lund Cathedral</a>, located in Sweden's southernmost and originally Danish province of <a href="/wiki/Scania" title="Scania">Scania</a>. He celebrated an ecumenical liturgy together with the president of the <a href="/wiki/Lutheran_World_Federation" title="Lutheran World Federation">Lutheran World Federation</a> Bishop Dr. <a href="/wiki/Munib_Younan" title="Munib Younan">Munib Younan</a>. A treaty aims for these two "branches" of <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> to in the future more see what unites than differs between them. (Pope Francis previously made a similar treaty with the Orthodox Church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[138]</a></sup>) The following day the Pope conducted a Catholic mass at a football stadium in <a href="/wiki/Malm%C3%B6" title="Malmö">Malmö</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[139]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mark_Hanson" title="Mark Hanson">Mark Hanson</a>, then presiding bishop of the <a href="/wiki/Evangelical_Lutheran_Church_in_America" title="Evangelical Lutheran Church in America">Evangelical Lutheran Church in America</a> (ELCA), greeted the news of Bergoglio's election with a public statement that praised his work with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutheran" title="Lutheran">Lutherans</a> in Argentina.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lutherans_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-lutherans-145">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evangelicalism">Evangelicalism</span></h3>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evangelical_Christian" title="Evangelical Christian">Evangelical Christian</a> leaders, including Argentine <a href="/wiki/Luis_Palau" title="Luis Palau">Luis Palau</a>, welcomed the news of Bergoglio's election as Pope based on his relations with <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">Evangelical Protestants</a>, noting that Bergoglio's financial manager for the Archdiocese of Buenos Aires was an Evangelical Christian whom Bergoglio refers to as a friend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-evangelicals_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-evangelicals-146">[141]</a></sup> Palau recounted how Bergoglio would not only relax and "drink <a href="/wiki/Mate_(beverage)" title="Mate (beverage)">mate</a>" with that friend, but would also read the Bible and pray with him, based on what Bergoglio called a relationship of friendship and trust.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-evangelicals_146-1"><a href="#cite_note-evangelicals-146">[141]</a></sup> Palau described Bergoglio's approach to relationships with Evangelicals as one of "building bridges and showing respect, knowing the differences, but majoring on what we can agree on: on the divinity of Jesus, his virgin birth, his resurrection, the second coming."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-evangelicals_146-2"><a href="#cite_note-evangelicals-146">[141]</a></sup> As a result of Bergoglio's election, Palau predicted that "tensions will be eased."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-evangelicals_146-3"><a href="#cite_note-evangelicals-146">[141]</a></sup></p>
<p>Juan Pablo Bongarrá, president of the Argentine Bible Society, recounted that Bergoglio not only met with Evangelicals and prayed with them, he also asked them to pray <i>for</i> him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weber_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-weber-147">[142]</a></sup> Bongarrá noted that Bergoglio would frequently end a conversation with the request, "Pastor, pray for me."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weber_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-weber-147">[142]</a></sup> Additionally, Bongarrá told the story of a weekly worship meeting of charismatic pastors in Buenos Aires, which Bergoglio attended: "He mounted the platform and called for pastors to pray for him. He knelt in front of nearly 6,000 people, and [the Protestant leaders there] laid hands and prayed."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weber_147-2"><a href="#cite_note-weber-147">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>Other Evangelical Christian leaders agreed that Bergoglio's relationships in Argentina made him "situated to better understand Protestantism" than had his predecessor Pope Benedict, "who often referred to Protestantism as a 'sect' of Christianity".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-christianitytoday_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-christianitytoday-148">[143]</a></sup> Noting that the divide between Catholicism and Protestantism is often present among members of the same families in Argentina, and is therefore an extremely important human issue, Evangelical author Chris Castaldo said that Francis could set the tone for more compassionate conversations among families about the differences between Protestantism and Catholicism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-christianitytoday_148-1"><a href="#cite_note-christianitytoday-148">[143]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Interfaith_dialogue">Interfaith dialogue</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pope_Francis_visit_Bethlehem.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3648" data-file-width="5472" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Pope_Francis_visit_Bethlehem.jpg/220px-Pope_Francis_visit_Bethlehem.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Pope_Francis_visit_Bethlehem.jpg/330px-Pope_Francis_visit_Bethlehem.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Pope_Francis_visit_Bethlehem.jpg/440px-Pope_Francis_visit_Bethlehem.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pope_Francis_visit_Bethlehem.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pope Francis in <a href="/wiki/Bethlehem" title="Bethlehem">Bethlehem</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a>, 25 May 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bergoglio has written about his commitment to open and respectful interfaith dialogue as a way for all parties engaged in that dialogue to learn from one another.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interfaith_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-interfaith-149">[144]</a></sup> In the 2011 book that records his conversations with Rabbi <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Skorka" title="Abraham Skorka">Abraham Skorka</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/On_Heaven_and_Earth" title="On Heaven and Earth">On Heaven and Earth</a></i>, Bergoglio said:</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Dialogue is born from an attitude of respect for the other person, from a conviction that the other person has something good to say. It assumes that there is room in the heart for the person's point of view, opinion, and proposal. Dialogue entails a cordial reception, not a prior condemnation. In order to dialogue it is necessary to know how to lower the defenses, open the doors of the house, and offer human warmth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interfaith_149-1"><a href="#cite_note-interfaith-149">[144]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Religious leaders in Buenos Aires have mentioned that Bergoglio promoted interfaith ceremonies at the <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires_Metropolitan_Cathedral" title="Buenos Aires Metropolitan Cathedral">Buenos Aires Metropolitan Cathedral</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ceremonies_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-ceremonies-150">[145]</a></sup> For example, in November 2012 he brought leaders of the Jewish, Muslim, Evangelical, and Orthodox Christian faiths together to pray for a peaceful solution to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_modern_conflicts_in_the_Middle_East" title="List of modern conflicts in the Middle East">Middle East conflicts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ceremonies_150-1"><a href="#cite_note-ceremonies-150">[145]</a></sup> Rabbi <a href="/wiki/Alejandro_Avruj" title="Alejandro Avruj">Alejandro Avruj</a> praised Bergoglio's interest in interfaith dialogue and his commitment to mend religious divisions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ceremonies_150-2"><a href="#cite_note-ceremonies-150">[145]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shortly after his election, the pope called for more interreligious dialogue as a way of "building bridges" and establishing "true links of friendship between all people".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interfaithdialogue_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-interfaithdialogue-151">[146]</a></sup> He added that it was crucial "to intensify outreach to nonbelievers, so that the differences which divide and hurt us may never prevail".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interfaithdialogue_151-1"><a href="#cite_note-interfaithdialogue-151">[146]</a></sup> He said that his title of "pontiff" means "builder of bridges", and that it was his wish that "the dialogue between us should help to build bridges connecting all people, in such a way that everyone can see in the other not an enemy, not a rival, but a brother or sister to be welcomed and embraced."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interfaithdialogue_151-2"><a href="#cite_note-interfaithdialogue-151">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 24 May 2014, Pope Francis arrived in <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a>, at the start of a tour of the Middle East, "aiming to boost ties with Muslims and Jews as well as easing an age-old rift within Christianity".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[147]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a 2016 survey, Francis was viewed favourably by almost two thirds of Jews, as well as majorities of Protestants and the irreligious; minorities of Buddhists and Muslims had favourable views of him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judaism">Judaism</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
