<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Franciscus_kotel.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="539" data-file-width="799" height="148" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Franciscus_kotel.jpg/220px-Franciscus_kotel.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Franciscus_kotel.jpg/330px-Franciscus_kotel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Franciscus_kotel.jpg/440px-Franciscus_kotel.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Franciscus_kotel.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Francis praying at the <a href="/wiki/Western_Wall" title="Western Wall">Western Wall</a> in <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> on his 2014 visit to the Holy Land</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bergoglio has close ties to the <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Argentina" title="History of the Jews in Argentina">Jewish community of Argentina</a>, and attended <a href="/wiki/Rosh_Hashanah" title="Rosh Hashanah">Rosh Hashanah</a> (Jewish new year) services in 2007 at a synagogue in Buenos Aires. He told the Jewish congregation during his visit that he went to the synagogue to examine his heart, "like a pilgrim, together with you, my elder brothers".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jta_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-jta-154">[149]</a></sup> After the 1994 <a href="/wiki/AMIA_bombing" title="AMIA bombing">AMIA bombing</a> of a <a href="/wiki/Jewish_Community_Center" title="Jewish Community Center">Jewish Community Center</a> that killed 85 people, Bergoglio was the first public figure to sign a petition condemning the attack and calling for justice. Jewish community leaders around the world noted that his words and actions "showed solidarity with the Jewish community" in the aftermath of this attack.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jta_154-1"><a href="#cite_note-jta-154">[149]</a></sup></p>
<p>A former head of the <a href="/wiki/World_Jewish_Congress" title="World Jewish Congress">World Jewish Congress</a>, <a href="/wiki/Israel_Singer" title="Israel Singer">Israel Singer</a>, reported that he worked with Bergoglio in the early 2000s, distributing aid to the poor as part of a joint Jewish–Catholic program called "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tzedak%C3%A1" title="Tzedaká">Tzedaká</a>". Singer noted that he was impressed with Bergoglio's modesty, remembering that "if everyone sat in chairs with handles [arms], he would sit in the one without."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jta_154-2"><a href="#cite_note-jta-154">[149]</a></sup> Bergoglio also co-hosted a <i><a href="/wiki/Kristallnacht" title="Kristallnacht">Kristallnacht</a></i> memorial ceremony at the <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires_Metropolitan_Cathedral" title="Buenos Aires Metropolitan Cathedral">Buenos Aires Metropolitan Cathedral</a> in 2012,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jta_154-3"><a href="#cite_note-jta-154">[149]</a></sup> and joined a group of clerics from a number of different religions to light candles in a 2012 synagogue ceremony on the occasion of the Jewish festival of <a href="/wiki/Hanukkah" title="Hanukkah">Hanukkah</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[150]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pope Francis blessed the cornerstone for the building of the museum devoted to <a href="/wiki/Rescue_of_Jews_by_Poles_during_the_Holocaust" title="Rescue of Jews by Poles during the Holocaust">wartime Polish rescuers of Jews</a> which is being built in the Polish village of <a href="/wiki/Markowa" title="Markowa">Markowa</a>; where the family of <a href="/wiki/J%C3%B3zef_and_Wiktoria_Ulma" title="Józef and Wiktoria Ulma">Józef and Wiktoria Ulma</a>, who are now <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Servants_of_God" title="Servants of God">Servants of God</a> as the Vatican is studying their cause for sainthood, were shot by the Germans for hiding their Jewish neighbors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[151]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Abraham_Skorka" title="Abraham Skorka">Abraham Skorka</a>, the rector of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin-American_Rabbinical_Seminary" title="Latin-American Rabbinical Seminary">Latin-American Rabbinical Seminary</a> in Buenos Aires, and Bergoglio published their conversations on religious and philosophical subjects as <i>Sobre el cielo y la tierra</i> (<i><a href="/wiki/On_Heaven_and_Earth" title="On Heaven and Earth">On Heaven and Earth</a></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jerusalempost_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-jerusalempost-157">[152]</a></sup> An editorial in <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jerusalem_Post" title="Jerusalem Post">Jerusalem Post</a></i> notes that "Unlike John Paul II, who as a child had positive memories of the Jews of his native Poland but due to the Holocaust had no Jewish community to interact with in Poland as an adult, Pope Francis has maintained a sustained and very positive relationship with a living, breathing [Jewish] community in Buenos Aires."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jerusalempost_157-1"><a href="#cite_note-jerusalempost-157">[152]</a></sup></p>
<p>One of the pope's first official actions was writing a letter to Rabbi <a href="/wiki/Riccardo_Di_Segni" title="Riccardo Di Segni">Riccardo Di Segni</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Rabbi" title="Chief Rabbi">Chief Rabbi</a> of Rome, inviting him to the papal installation and sharing his hope of collaboration between the Catholic and Jewish communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-romerabbi_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-romerabbi-158">[153]</a></sup> Addressing representatives of Jewish organizations and communities, Francis said that, "due to our common roots [a] Christian cannot be <a href="/wiki/Antisemitism" title="Antisemitism">anti-Semitic</a>!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[154]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islam">Islam</span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Argentina" title="Islam in Argentina">Muslim leaders in Buenos Aires</a> welcomed the news of Bergoglio's election as pope, noting that he "always showed himself as a friend of the Islamic community", and a person whose position is "pro-dialogue".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-islam_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-islam-160">[155]</a></sup> They praised Bergoglio's close ties with Muslim groups and noted his comments when Pope Benedict's 2006 <a href="/wiki/Regensburg_lecture" title="Regensburg lecture">Regensburg lecture</a> was interpreted by many as denigrating Islam. According to them, Bergoglio immediately distanced himself from Benedict's language and said that statements which provoked outrage with Muslims would "serve to destroy in 20 seconds the careful construction of a relationship with Islam that Pope John Paul II built over the last 20 years."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-muslim_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-muslim-161">[156]</a></sup></p>
<p>Bergoglio visited both a mosque and an Islamic school in Argentina; visits that the Director for the Diffusion of Islam, Sheik Mohsen Ali, called actions that strengthened the relationship between the Catholic and Islamic communities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-islam_160-1"><a href="#cite_note-islam-160">[155]</a></sup> Sumer Noufouri, Secretary General of the Islamic Center of the Argentine Republic (CIRA), added that for Muslims, Bergoglio's past actions make his election as pope a cause of "joy and expectation of strengthening dialogue between religions".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-islam_160-2"><a href="#cite_note-islam-160">[155]</a></sup> Noufouri said that the relationship between CIRA and Bergoglio over the course of a decade had helped to build up Christian–Muslim dialogue in a way that was "really significant in the history of monotheistic relations in Argentina".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-islam_160-3"><a href="#cite_note-islam-160">[155]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ahmed_el-Tayeb" title="Ahmed el-Tayeb">Ahmed el-Tayeb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grand_Imam_of_al-Azhar" title="Grand Imam of al-Azhar">Grand Imam of al-Azhar</a> and president of Egypt's <a href="/wiki/Al-Azhar_University" title="Al-Azhar University">Al-Azhar University</a>, sent congratulations after the pope's election.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-asia_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-asia-162">[157]</a></sup> Al-Tayeb had "broken off relations with the Vatican" during Benedict XVI's time as pope; his message of congratulations also included the request that "Islam asks for respect from the new pontiff".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-asia_162-1"><a href="#cite_note-asia-162">[157]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shortly after his election, in a meeting with ambassadors from the 180 countries accredited with the Holy See, Pope Francis called for more interreligious dialogue—"particularly with Islam".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interfaithdialogue_151-3"><a href="#cite_note-interfaithdialogue-151">[146]</a></sup> He also expressed gratitude that "so many civil and religious leaders from the Islamic world" had attended his installation Mass.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-interfaithdialogue_151-4"><a href="#cite_note-interfaithdialogue-151">[146]</a></sup> An editorial in the Saudi Arabian paper <i><a href="/wiki/Saudi_Gazette" title="Saudi Gazette">Saudi Gazette</a></i> strongly welcomed the pope's call for increased interfaith dialogue, stressing that while the pope was "reiterating a position he has always maintained", his public call as pope for increased dialogue with Islam "comes as a breath of fresh air at a time when much of the Western world is experiencing a nasty outbreak of <a href="/wiki/Islamophobia" title="Islamophobia">Islamophobia</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-saudigazette_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-saudigazette-163">[158]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2016, Pope Francis met with Ahmed el-Tayeb at the Vatican, the first meeting since 2000 between the Grand Imam of al-Azhar and the leader of the world's Catholics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-meetingahmed_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-meetingahmed-164">[159]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Attitudes_about_non-believers">Attitudes about non-believers</span></h2>
<p>Speaking to journalists and media employees on 16 March 2013, Pope Francis said he would bless them silently, "Given that many of you do not belong to the Catholic Church, and others are not believers."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[160]</a></sup> In his papal address on 20 March, he said the "attempt to eliminate God and the Divine from the horizon of humanity" resulted in violence, but described as well his feelings about nonbelievers: "[W]e also sense our closeness to all those men and women who, although not identifying themselves as followers of any religious tradition, are nonetheless searching for truth, goodness and beauty, the truth, goodness and beauty of God. They are our valued allies in the commitment to defending human dignity, in building a peaceful coexistence between peoples and in safeguarding and caring for creation."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[161]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[162]</a></sup></p>
<p>Some atheists expressed hope that Francis would prove to be progressive on issues like poverty and social inequality,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[163]</a></sup> while others were more skeptical that he would be "interested in a partnership of equals".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[164]</a></sup> In May 2013, Francis said that all who do good can be <a href="/wiki/Redemption_(theology)#Christianity" title="Redemption (theology)">redeemed</a> through Jesus, including atheists. Francis stated that God "has redeemed all of us, all of us, with the Blood of Christ: all of us, not just Catholics. Everyone! Even the atheists, Everyone!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[165]</a></sup> Amid the controversy that ensued, <a href="/wiki/Carl_E._Olson" title="Carl E. Olson">Carl E. Olson</a> pointed out that Francis' words were fundamental Christian teaching dating back to the Apostle Paul<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[166]</a></sup> and Fr. Dwight Longenecker wrote, "Unfortunately for those who wish to paint Pope Francis as a lovable liberal, in fact, the Pope is simply affirming certain truths that any somewhat knowledgable Catholic will uphold."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[167]</a></sup> A spokesman for the Vatican, Father <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Rosica" title="Thomas Rosica">Thomas Rosica</a>, issued an "explanatory note" that non-Catholics who "know" the Roman Catholic Church but do not convert "cannot be saved", and only those who "sincerely seek God ... can attain eternal salvation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[168]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hendrik_Hertzberg" title="Hendrik Hertzberg">Hendrik Hertzberg</a> criticised Rosica in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i> magazine, and speculated that there may be major internal disagreement between supporters and opponents of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vatican_II" title="Vatican II">Vatican II</a> in the Catholic Church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[169]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2013, Francis wrote an open letter to the founder of <i><a href="/wiki/La_Repubblica" title="La Repubblica">La Repubblica</a></i> newspaper, <a href="/wiki/Eugenio_Scalfari" title="Eugenio Scalfari">Eugenio Scalfari</a>, stating that non-believers would be forgiven by God if they followed their <a href="/wiki/Conscience" title="Conscience">consciences</a>. Responding to a list of questions published in the paper by Scalfari, who is not a Roman Catholic, Francis wrote: "You ask me if the God of the Christians forgives those who don't believe and who don't seek the faith. I start by saying—and this is the fundamental thing—that God's mercy has no limits if you go to him with a sincere and contrite heart. The issue for those who do not believe in God is to obey their conscience. Sin, even for those who have no faith, exists when people disobey their conscience."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[170]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Papacy_.282013.E2.80.93present.29">Papacy (2013–present)</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tmulti tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:271px;max-width:271px">
<div style="clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;background-color:transparent"><a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Pope_Francis" title="Coat of arms of Pope Francis">Coat of arms of Pope Francis</a></div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:152px;max-width:152px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coat_of_arms_of_Jorge_Mario_Bergoglio.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1218" data-file-width="1148" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Coat_of_arms_of_Jorge_Mario_Bergoglio.svg/150px-Coat_of_arms_of_Jorge_Mario_Bergoglio.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Coat_of_arms_of_Jorge_Mario_Bergoglio.svg/225px-Coat_of_arms_of_Jorge_Mario_Bergoglio.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Coat_of_arms_of_Jorge_Mario_Bergoglio.svg/300px-Coat_of_arms_of_Jorge_Mario_Bergoglio.svg.png 2x" width="150"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">As Cardinal</div>
</div>
<div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:115px;max-width:115px">
<div class="thumbimage"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Insigne_Francisci.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="1120" data-file-width="800" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Insigne_Francisci.svg/113px-Insigne_Francisci.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Insigne_Francisci.svg/170px-Insigne_Francisci.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Insigne_Francisci.svg/226px-Insigne_Francisci.svg.png 2x" width="113"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:center">As Pope</div>
</div>
<div style="clear:left"></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left;text-align:left;background-color:transparent">The gold star represents the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virgin_Mary" title="Virgin Mary">Virgin Mary</a>, the grape-like plant—the <a href="/wiki/Spikenard" title="Spikenard">spikenard</a>—is associated with <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph" title="Saint Joseph">Saint Joseph</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Name_of_Jesus" title="Holy Name of Jesus">IHS</a> emblem is the symbol of the Jesuits<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[171]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[172]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NCR_178-0"><a href="#cite_note-NCR-178">[173]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Elected at the age of 76, Francis was reported to be healthy and his doctors have stated that his missing lung tissue, removed in his youth, does not have a significant impact on his health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pope_Francis.27s_missing_lung_should_not_be_a_problem.2C_say_doctors_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pope_Francis.27s_missing_lung_should_not_be_a_problem.2C_say_doctors-179">[174]</a></sup> The only concern would be decreased respiratory reserve if he had a respiratory infection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Why_Pope_Francis_Only_Has_One_Lung_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-Why_Pope_Francis_Only_Has_One_Lung-180">[175]</a></sup> In the past, one attack of <a href="/wiki/Sciatica" title="Sciatica">sciatica</a> in 2007 prevented him from attending a consistory and delayed his return to Argentina for several days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-falasca_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-falasca-76">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Francis is the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit" title="Jesuit">Jesuit</a> pope. This was an unexpected appointment, because of the tense relations between the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Society of Jesus</a> and the Holy See.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[176]</a></sup> He is also the first from the Americas,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[177]</a></sup> and the first from the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a>. Many media reported him as being the first non-European pope, but he is actually the 11th. The previous one was from Syria, <a href="/wiki/Pope_Gregory_III" title="Pope Gregory III">Gregory III</a> in 741; 1,272 years earlier. However, although Francis does not have a European nationality, he has a European ethnicity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[178]</a></sup></p>
<p>As pope, his manner is less formal than that of his predecessors: a style that news coverage has referred to as "no frills," noting that it is "his common touch and accessibility that is proving the greatest inspiration."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nofrills_184-0"><a href="#cite_note-nofrills-184">[179]</a></sup> On the night of his election, he took the bus back to his hotel with the cardinals, rather than be driven in the papal car.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[180]</a></sup> The next day, he visited Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Mar%C3%ADa_Mej%C3%ADa" title="Jorge María Mejía">Jorge María Mejía</a> in the hospital and chatted with patients and staff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[181]</a></sup> At his first media audience, the Friday after his election, the Pope said of Saint Francis of Assisi: "The man who gives us this spirit of peace, the poor man", and he added "[h]ow I would like a poor Church, and for the poor".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[182]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_language" title="Native language">native</a> Spanish, Francis is also conversant in Latin (the <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> of the Holy See), he speaks fluent Italian, (the official language of Vatican City and the "everyday language" of the Holy See), German,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[183]</a></sup> French,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[184]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[185]</a></sup> English,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[186]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-languages_192-0"><a href="#cite_note-languages-192">[187]</a></sup> and he understands the <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">Piedmontese language</a> and some <a href="/wiki/Genoese_dialect" title="Genoese dialect">Genoese</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[188]</a></sup></p>
<p>Francis chose not to live in the official <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papal_apartments" title="Papal apartments">papal residence</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Palace" title="Apostolic Palace">Apostolic Palace</a>, but to remain in the <a href="/wiki/Domus_Sanctae_Marthae" title="Domus Sanctae Marthae">Vatican guest house</a>, in a suite in which he can receive visitors and hold meetings. He is the first pope since <a href="/wiki/Pope_Pius_X" title="Pope Pius X">Pope Pius X</a> to live outside the papal apartments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vatican_guesthouse_194-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vatican_guesthouse-194">[189]</a></sup> Francis still appears at the window of the Apostolic Palace for the Sunday <a href="/wiki/Angelus" title="Angelus">Angelus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guesthouse_195-0"><a href="#cite_note-guesthouse-195">[190]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Election">Election</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Papal_conclave,_2013" title="Papal conclave, 2013">Papal conclave, 2013</a> and <a href="/wiki/Papal_inauguration_of_Pope_Francis" title="Papal inauguration of Pope Francis">Papal inauguration of Pope Francis</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Papa_Francisco_reci%C3%A9n_elegido_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="704" data-file-width="1004" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Papa_Francisco_reci%C3%A9n_elegido_2.jpg/220px-Papa_Francisco_reci%C3%A9n_elegido_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Papa_Francisco_reci%C3%A9n_elegido_2.jpg/330px-Papa_Francisco_reci%C3%A9n_elegido_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Papa_Francisco_reci%C3%A9n_elegido_2.jpg/440px-Papa_Francisco_reci%C3%A9n_elegido_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Papa_Francisco_reci%C3%A9n_elegido_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Francis appears to the public for the first time as pope, at the balcony of St. Peter's Basilica, 13 March 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bergoglio was elected pope on 13 March 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-directory_5-8"><a href="#cite_note-directory-5">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[191]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[192]</a></sup> the second day of the <a href="/wiki/Papal_conclave,_2013" title="Papal conclave, 2013">2013 papal conclave</a>, taking the <a href="/wiki/Papal_name" title="Papal name">papal name</a> Francis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-directory_5-9"><a href="#cite_note-directory-5">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnbc_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnbc-198">[193]</a></sup> Francis was elected on the fifth ballot of the conclave.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[194]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Habemus_Papam" title="Habemus Papam">Habemus Papam</a> was delivered by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardinal_protodeacon" title="Cardinal protodeacon">Cardinal protodeacon</a> <a href="/wiki/Jean-Louis_Tauran" title="Jean-Louis Tauran">Jean-Louis Tauran</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SuarezPBS_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-SuarezPBS-200">[195]</a></sup> Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Christoph_Sch%C3%B6nborn" title="Christoph Schönborn">Christoph Schönborn</a> later said that Bergoglio was elected following two supernatural signs, one in the conclave and hence confidential, and a Latin-American couple of friends of Schönborn who whispered Bergoglio's name in Schönborn's ear; Schönborn commented "if these people say Bergoglio, that's an indication of the Holy Spirit".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[196]</a></sup></p>
<p>Instead of accepting his cardinals' congratulations while seated on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papal_throne" title="Papal throne">Papal throne</a>, Francis received them standing, reportedly an immediate sign of a changing approach to formalities at the Vatican.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewEuropeHabemus_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-NewEuropeHabemus-202">[197]</a></sup> During his first appearance as pontiff on the balcony of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Peter%27s_Basilica" title="Saint Peter's Basilica">Saint Peter's Basilica</a>, he wore a white <a href="/wiki/Cassock" title="Cassock">cassock</a>, not the red, ermine-trimmed <a href="/wiki/Mozzetta" title="Mozzetta">mozzetta</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NewEuropeHabemus_202-1"><a href="#cite_note-NewEuropeHabemus-202">[197]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Uebbing_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-Uebbing-203">[198]</a></sup> used by the previous Popes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[199]</a></sup> He also wore the same iron <a href="/wiki/Pectoral_cross" title="Pectoral cross">pectoral cross</a> that he had worn as Archbishop of Buenos Aires, rather than the gold one worn by his predecessors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Uebbing_203-1"><a href="#cite_note-Uebbing-203">[198]</a></sup></p>
<p>After being elected and choosing his name, his first act was bestowing the <i><a href="/wiki/Urbi_et_Orbi" title="Urbi et Orbi">Urbi et Orbi</a></i> blessing to thousands of pilgrims gathered in <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Square" title="St. Peter's Square">St. Peter's Square</a>. Before blessing the crowd, he asked those in St. Peter's Square to pray for his predecessor, Pope Emeritus Benedict XVI, and for himself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[200]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pope Francis held his <a href="/wiki/Papal_inauguration" title="Papal inauguration">Papal inauguration</a> on 19 March 2013 in <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Square" title="St. Peter's Square">St. Peter's Square</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-directory_5-10"><a href="#cite_note-directory-5">[3]</a></sup> He celebrated Mass in the presence of various political and religious leaders from around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[201]</a></sup> In his homily Pope Francis focused on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solemnity_of_Saint_Joseph" title="Solemnity of Saint Joseph">Solemnity of Saint Joseph</a>, the liturgical day on which the Mass was celebrated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[202]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pope_Francis_among_the_people_at_St._Peter%27s_Square_-_12_May_2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Pope_Francis_among_the_people_at_St._Peter%27s_Square_-_12_May_2013.jpg/220px-Pope_Francis_among_the_people_at_St._Peter%27s_Square_-_12_May_2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Pope_Francis_among_the_people_at_St._Peter%27s_Square_-_12_May_2013.jpg/330px-Pope_Francis_among_the_people_at_St._Peter%27s_Square_-_12_May_2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Pope_Francis_among_the_people_at_St._Peter%27s_Square_-_12_May_2013.jpg/440px-Pope_Francis_among_the_people_at_St._Peter%27s_Square_-_12_May_2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pope_Francis_among_the_people_at_St._Peter%27s_Square_-_12_May_2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Francis among the people at <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Square" title="St. Peter's Square">St. Peter's Square</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At his first audience on 16 March 2013, Francis told journalists that he had chosen the name in honor of <a href="/wiki/Francis_of_Assisi" title="Francis of Assisi">Saint Francis of Assisi</a>, and had done so because he was especially concerned for the well-being of the poor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pope_Francis_explains_decision_to_take_St_Francis_of_Assisi.27s_name_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pope_Francis_explains_decision_to_take_St_Francis_of_Assisi.27s_name-208">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Pope_Francis_visits_St._Mary_Major.2C_collects_suitcases_and_pays_bill_at_hotel_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-New_Pope_Francis_visits_St._Mary_Major.2C_collects_suitcases_and_pays_bill_at_hotel-209">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[205]</a></sup> He explained that, as it was becoming clear during the conclave voting that he would be elected the new bishop of Rome, the Brazilian Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Cl%C3%A1udio_Hummes" title="Cláudio Hummes">Cláudio Hummes</a> had embraced him and whispered, "Don't forget the poor", which had made Bergoglio think of the saint.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-211"><a href="#cite_note-211">[206]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[207]</a></sup> Bergoglio had previously expressed his admiration for St. Francis, explaining that "He brought to Christianity an idea of poverty against the luxury, pride, vanity of the civil and ecclesiastical powers of the time. He changed history."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bethune_213-0"><a href="#cite_note-bethune-213">[208]</a></sup></p>
<p>This is the first time that a pope has been named <i>Francis</i>. On the day of his election, the Vatican clarified that his official papal name was "Francis", not "Francis I", i.e. no <a href="/wiki/Regnal_number" title="Regnal number">regnal number</a> is used for him. A Vatican spokesman said that the name would become Francis I if and when there is a Francis II.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_Pope_Francis_visits_St._Mary_Major.2C_collects_suitcases_and_pays_bill_at_hotel_209-1"><a href="#cite_note-New_Pope_Francis_visits_St._Mary_Major.2C_collects_suitcases_and_pays_bill_at_hotel-209">[204]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vatican:_It.27s_Pope_Francis.2C_not_Pope_Francis_I_214-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vatican:_It.27s_Pope_Francis.2C_not_Pope_Francis_I-214">[209]</a></sup> It is the first time since <a href="/wiki/Pope_Lando" title="Pope Lando">Pope Lando</a>'s 913–914 reign that a serving pope holds a name not used by a predecessor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[f]</a></sup></p>
<p>Francis also said that some cardinal-electors had jokingly suggested to him that he should choose either "Adrian", since <a href="/wiki/Pope_Adrian_VI" title="Pope Adrian VI">Pope Adrian VI</a> had been a reformer of the church, or "Clement" to settle the score with <a href="/wiki/Pope_Clement_XIV" title="Pope Clement XIV">Pope Clement XIV</a>, who had <a href="/wiki/Suppression_of_the_Society_of_Jesus" title="Suppression of the Society of Jesus">suppressed the Jesuit order</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-217"><a href="#cite_note-217">[211]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-218"><a href="#cite_note-218">[212]</a></sup> In February 2014, it was reported that Bergoglio, had he been elected in 2005, would have chosen the pontifical name of "John XXIV" in honor of <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_XXIII" title="Pope John XXIII">Pope John XXIII</a>. It was said that he told Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Francesco_Marchisano" title="Francesco Marchisano">Francesco Marchisano</a>: "John, I would have called myself John, like the Good Pope; I would have been completely inspired by him".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-219"><a href="#cite_note-219">[213]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Curia">Curia</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Francis_Inauguration_fc10.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Francis_Inauguration_fc10.jpg/220px-Francis_Inauguration_fc10.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Francis_Inauguration_fc10.jpg/330px-Francis_Inauguration_fc10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Francis_Inauguration_fc10.jpg/440px-Francis_Inauguration_fc10.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Francis_Inauguration_fc10.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Inauguration of Pope Francis, 19 March 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 16 March 2013, Pope Francis asked all those in senior positions of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Curia" title="Roman Curia">Roman Curia</a> to provisionally continue in office.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[214]</a></sup> He named <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Xuereb" title="Alfred Xuereb">Alfred Xuereb</a> as his personal secretary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-221"><a href="#cite_note-221">[215]</a></sup> On 6 April he named <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Rodr%C3%ADguez_Carballo" title="José Rodríguez Carballo">José Rodríguez Carballo</a> as secretary for the <a href="/wiki/Congregation_for_Institutes_of_Consecrated_Life_and_Societies_of_Apostolic_Life" title="Congregation for Institutes of Consecrated Life and Societies of Apostolic Life">Congregation for Institutes of Consecrated Life and Societies of Apostolic Life</a>, a position that had been vacant for several months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[216]</a></sup> Francis abolished the bonuses paid to Vatican employees upon the election of a new pope, amounting to several million Euros, opting instead to donate the money to charity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-223"><a href="#cite_note-223">[217]</a></sup> He also abolished the €25,000 annual bonus paid to the cardinals serving on the Board of Supervisors for the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_the_Works_of_Religion" title="Institute for the Works of Religion">Vatican bank</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[218]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 13 April 2013, he named eight cardinals to a new <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Cardinal_Advisers" title="Council of Cardinal Advisers">Council of Cardinal Advisers</a> to advise him on revising the organizational structure of the Roman Curia. The group included several known as critics of Vatican operations and only one member of the Curia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-225"><a href="#cite_note-225">[219]</a></sup> They are <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Bertello" title="Giuseppe Bertello">Giuseppe Bertello</a>, president of the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Pontifical_Commission_for_Vatican_City_State" title="President of the Pontifical Commission for Vatican City State">Vatican City State governorate</a>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francisco_Javier_Errazuriz_Ossa" title="Francisco Javier Errazuriz Ossa">Francisco Javier Errazuriz Ossa</a> from Chile; <a href="/wiki/Oswald_Gracias" title="Oswald Gracias">Oswald Gracias</a> from India; <a href="/wiki/Reinhard_Marx" title="Reinhard Marx">Reinhard Marx</a> from Germany; <a href="/wiki/Laurent_Monsengwo_Pasinya" title="Laurent Monsengwo Pasinya">Laurent Monsengwo Pasinya</a> from the Democratic Republic of the Congo; <a href="/wiki/George_Pell" title="George Pell">George Pell</a> from Australia; <a href="/wiki/Se%C3%A1n_Patrick_O%27Malley" title="Seán Patrick O'Malley">Seán O'Malley</a> from the United States; and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oscar_Andres_Rodriguez_Maradiaga" title="Oscar Andres Rodriguez Maradiaga">Oscar Andres Rodriguez Maradiaga</a> from Honduras. He appointed Bishop <a href="/wiki/Marcello_Semeraro" title="Marcello Semeraro">Marcello Semeraro</a> secretary for the group and scheduled its first meeting for 1–3 October.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[220]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_issues">Early issues</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pope_Francis_Travels.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="863" height="154" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Pope_Francis_Travels.svg/300px-Pope_Francis_Travels.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Pope_Francis_Travels.svg/450px-Pope_Francis_Travels.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Pope_Francis_Travels.svg/600px-Pope_Francis_Travels.svg.png 2x" width="300"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pope_Francis_Travels.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map indicating <a href="/wiki/List_of_pastoral_visits_of_Pope_Francis_outside_Italy" title="List of pastoral visits of Pope Francis outside Italy">countries visited by Francis as pope</a>, as of November 2016<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pope_Francis&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In March 2013, 21 British Catholic <a href="/wiki/House_of_Lords" title="House of Lords">peers</a> and <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">Members of Parliament</a> from all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_parties_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Political parties in the United Kingdom">parties</a> asked Francis to allow married men in Great Britain to be ordained as priests, keeping celibacy as the rule for bishops. They asked it on the grounds that it would be anomalous that married Anglican priests can be received into the Catholic Church and ordained as priests, by means of either the <a href="/wiki/Pastoral_Provision" title="Pastoral Provision">Pastoral Provision</a> of 20 June 1980 or the 2009 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglican_ordinariate" title="Anglican ordinariate">Anglican ordinariate</a>, but married Catholic men cannot do the same.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-teahan_227-0"><a href="#cite_note-teahan-227">[221]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Fouad_Twal" title="Fouad Twal">Fouad Twal</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_Patriarch_of_Jerusalem" title="Latin Patriarch of Jerusalem">Latin Patriarch of Jerusalem</a>, included a call in his 2013 Easter homily for the Pope to visit <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-228"><a href="#cite_note-228">[222]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_Rapha%C3%ABl_I_Sako" title="Louis Raphaël I Sako">Louis Raphael I</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chaldean_Catholic_Church" title="Chaldean Catholic Church">Chaldean Catholic Patriarch</a>, asked the Pope to visit the "embattled Christian community" in Iraq.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iraq_229-0"><a href="#cite_note-iraq-229">[223]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the first <a href="/wiki/Maundy_Thursday" title="Maundy Thursday">Holy Thursday</a> following his election, Francis washed and kissed the feet of ten male and two female juvenile offenders, not all Catholic, aged from 14 to 21, imprisoned at Rome's Casal del Marmo detention facility, telling them <a href="/wiki/Foot_washing" title="Foot washing">the ritual of foot washing</a> is a sign that he is at their service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-muslimfeetwashing_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-muslimfeetwashing-230">[224]</a></sup> This was the first time that a pope had included women in this ritual; although he had already done so when he was archbishop.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-muslimfeetwashing_230-1"><a href="#cite_note-muslimfeetwashing-230">[224]</a></sup> One of the male and one of the female offenders was a <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-muslimfeetwashing_230-2"><a href="#cite_note-muslimfeetwashing-230">[224]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[225]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 31 March 2013 Francis used his first <a href="/wiki/Urbi_et_Orbi" title="Urbi et Orbi">Easter homily</a> to make a plea for peace throughout the world, specifically mentioning the Middle East, Africa, and North and South Korea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eastersermon_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-eastersermon-232">[226]</a></sup> He also spoke out against those who give in to "easy gain" in a world filled with greed, and made a plea for humanity to become a better guardian of creation by protecting the environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eastersermon_232-1"><a href="#cite_note-eastersermon-232">[226]</a></sup> He said that "[w]e ask the risen Jesus, who turns death into life, to change hatred into love, vengeance into forgiveness, war into peace."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-risenjesus_233-0"><a href="#cite_note-risenjesus-233">[227]</a></sup> Although the Vatican had prepared greetings in 65 languages, Francis chose not to read them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-languages_192-1"><a href="#cite_note-languages-192">[187]</a></sup> According to the Vatican, the pope "at least for now, feels at ease using Italian, the everyday language of the Holy See".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[228]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, Francis initially reaffirmed the <a href="/wiki/Congregation_for_the_Doctrine_of_the_Faith" title="Congregation for the Doctrine of the Faith">Congregation for the Doctrine of the Faith</a>'s program to <a href="/wiki/Leadership_Conference_of_Women_Religious#Doctrinal_issues" title="Leadership Conference of Women Religious">reform the U.S. Leadership Conference of Women Religious</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-235"><a href="#cite_note-235">[229]</a></sup> initiated under his predecessor, Pope Benedict XVI. <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> reported that the Vatican had formed the opinion in 2012 that the sisters' group was tinged with feminist influences, focused too much on ending social and economic injustice and not enough on stopping abortion, and permitted speakers at its meetings who questioned church doctrine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-236"><a href="#cite_note-236">[230]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-237"><a href="#cite_note-237">[231]</a></sup> However, in April 2015 the investigation was brought to a close. The timing of the closure may have anticipated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pope_Francis%27_visit_to_the_United_States" title="Pope Francis' visit to the United States">a visit by Francis to the U.S.</a> in September 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[232]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 12 May, Francis carried out his first <a href="/wiki/Canonization" title="Canonization">canonizations</a> of candidates approved for sainthood during the reign of Benedict XVI: the first Colombian saint, <a href="/wiki/Laura_of_Saint_Catherine_of_Siena" title="Laura of Saint Catherine of Siena">Laura of Saint Catherine of Siena</a>, the second female Mexican saint, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maria_Guadalupe_Garcia_Zavala" title="Maria Guadalupe Garcia Zavala">Maria Guadalupe Garcia Zavala</a>, both of the 20th century, and the 813 15th-century <a href="/wiki/Martyrs_of_Otranto" title="Martyrs of Otranto">Martyrs of Otranto</a>. He said: "While we venerate the martyrs of Otranto, ask God to support the many Christians who still suffer from violence and give them the courage and fate and respond to evil with goodness." He also commented on abortion, saying legislation should be introduced to "protect all human beings from the first moment of their existence."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[233]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consultation_with_Catholic_laity">Consultation with Catholic laity</span></h3>
<p>A February 2014 survey by <a href="/wiki/World_Values_Survey" title="World Values Survey">World Values Survey</a> cited in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> shows how the unity Pope Francis had created could be challenged. Although views about Francis personally were favorable, many Catholics disagreed with at least some of his teachings. The survey found that members of the Roman Catholic Church are deeply divided over abortion, artificial contraception, divorce, the ordination of women, and married priests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[234]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-241"><a href="#cite_note-241">[235]</a></sup> In the same month Pope Francis asked parishes to provide answers to an official questionnaire<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[236]</a></sup> described as a "much broader consultation than just a survey"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc27060172_243-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc27060172-243">[237]</a></sup> regarding opinions among the laity. He continued to assert <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic_doctrine" title="Catholic doctrine">Catholic doctrine</a>, in less dramatic tone than his recent predecessors, who maintained that the Catholic Church is not a democracy of popular opinion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clement_244-0"><a href="#cite_note-Clement-244">[238]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Linda_Woodhead" title="Linda Woodhead">Linda Woodhead</a> of <a href="/wiki/Lancaster_University" title="Lancaster University">Lancaster University</a> wrote of the survey Francis initiated, "it's not a survey in any sense that a social scientist would recognize." Woodhead said that many ordinary Catholics would have difficulty understanding theological <a href="/wiki/Jargon" title="Jargon">jargon</a> there. Nonetheless, she suspected the survey might be influential.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[239]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_in_England_and_Wales" title="Catholic Church in England and Wales">Catholic Church in England and Wales</a> as of April 2014<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Pope_Francis&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> had refused to publish results of this survey; a Church spokesman said a senior Vatican official had expressly asked for summaries to remain confidential, and that orders had come from the Pope that the information should not be made public until after October. This disappointed many reformers who hoped the laity would be more involved in decision-making. Some other Roman Catholic churches, for example in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Germany" title="Roman Catholicism in Germany">Germany</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism_in_Austria" title="Roman Catholicism in Austria">Austria</a>, published summaries of the responses to the survey, which showed a wide gap between Church teaching and the behavior of ordinary Catholics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc27060172_243-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc27060172-243">[237]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a column he wrote for the Vatican's semi-official newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/L%27Osservatore_Romano" title="L'Osservatore Romano">L'Osservatore Romano</a></i>, the head Prefect of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Supreme_Tribunal_of_the_Apostolic_Signatura" title="Supreme Tribunal of the Apostolic Signatura">Supreme Tribunal of the Apostolic Signatura</a>, US Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Leo_Burke" title="Raymond Leo Burke">Raymond Leo Burke</a>, who has a long-standing reputation as one of the church's most vocal conservative hard-liners, said that Pope Francis opposed both abortion and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gay_marriage" title="Gay marriage">gay marriage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[240]</a></sup> The Vatican's chief spokesman, Father <a href="/wiki/Federico_Lombardi" title="Federico Lombardi">Federico Lombardi</a>, also noted in the Vatican Press Office during the 2014 consistory meetings that Pope Francis and Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Walter_Kasper" title="Walter Kasper">Walter Kasper</a> would not change or redefine any dogmas pertaining to Church theology on doctrinal matters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-247"><a href="#cite_note-247">[241]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Institute_for_the_Works_of_Religion">Institute for the Works of Religion</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pope_Franciscus_in_Mus%C3%A9e_Gr%C3%A9vin.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3116" data-file-width="1210" height="322" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Pope_Franciscus_in_Mus%C3%A9e_Gr%C3%A9vin.jpg/125px-Pope_Franciscus_in_Mus%C3%A9e_Gr%C3%A9vin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Pope_Franciscus_in_Mus%C3%A9e_Gr%C3%A9vin.jpg/188px-Pope_Franciscus_in_Mus%C3%A9e_Gr%C3%A9vin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Pope_Franciscus_in_Mus%C3%A9e_Gr%C3%A9vin.jpg/250px-Pope_Franciscus_in_Mus%C3%A9e_Gr%C3%A9vin.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pope_Franciscus_in_Mus%C3%A9e_Gr%C3%A9vin.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Wax statue at <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_Gr%C3%A9vin" title="Musée Grévin">Musée Grévin</a>, Paris</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the first months of Francis' papacy, the <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_the_Works_of_Religion" title="Institute for the Works of Religion">Institute for the Works of Religion</a>, informally known as the Vatican Bank, said that it would become more transparent in its financial dealings<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[242]</a></sup> There had long been allegations of corruption and <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a> connected with the bank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bank1_249-0"><a href="#cite_note-bank1-249">[243]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bank2_250-0"><a href="#cite_note-bank2-250">[244]</a></sup> Francis appointed a commission to advise him about reform of the Bank,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bank1_249-1"><a href="#cite_note-bank1-249">[243]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bank2_250-1"><a href="#cite_note-bank2-250">[244]</a></sup> and the finance consulting firm <a href="/wiki/Promontory_Financial_Group" title="Promontory Financial Group">Promontory Financial Group</a> was assigned to carry out a comprehensive investigation of all customer contacts of the bank on these facts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[245]</a></sup> Because of this affair the <a href="/wiki/Devil%27s_advocate#Origin" title="Devil's advocate">Promoter of Justice</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Vatican_City" title="Law of Vatican City">Vatican Tribunal</a> applied a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Letter_rogatory" title="Letter rogatory">letter rogatory</a> for the first time in the history of the Republic of Italy at the beginning of August 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[246]</a></sup> In January 2014 Francis replaced four of the five cardinal overseers of the Vatican Bank, who had been confirmed in their positions in the final days of Benedict XVI's papacy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[247]</a></sup> Lay experts and clerics were looking into how the bank was run. <a href="/wiki/Ernst_von_Freyberg" title="Ernst von Freyberg">Ernst von Freyberg</a> was put in charge. <a href="/wiki/Moneyval" title="Moneyval">Moneyval</a> feels more reform is needed, and Francis may be willing to close the bank if the reforms prove too difficult.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jones_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jones-254">[248]</a></sup> There is uncertainty how far reforms can succeed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[249]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Papal_documents">Papal documents</span></h3>
<p>On 29 June 2013, Pope Francis published his first <a href="/wiki/Encyclical" title="Encyclical">encyclical</a>, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Lumen_fidei" title="Lumen fidei">Lumen fidei</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_Holy_See_256-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_Holy_See-256">[250]</a></sup> It is a <a href="/wiki/Collaborative_writing" title="Collaborative writing">collaborative writing</a> with Benedict XVI and talks about faith, complementing Benedict's previous encyclicals on charity and hope.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lumen_257-0"><a href="#cite_note-lumen-257">[251]</a></sup> He published his second one, entitled <span style="padding-right:0.1em;"><i><a href="/wiki/Laudato_si%27" title="Laudato si'">Laudato si'</a></i></span>, on 18 June 2015, concerning care for the planet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jim_Yardley_and_Laurie_Goodstein_258-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jim_Yardley_and_Laurie_Goodstein-258">[252]</a></sup> On 24 November 2013, he published his <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_exhortation" title="Apostolic exhortation">apostolic exhortation</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Evangelii_gaudium" title="Evangelii gaudium">Evangelii gaudium</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Evangelii_gaudium_259-0"><a href="#cite_note-Evangelii_gaudium-259">[253]</a></sup> with his views on <a href="#Faith_and_evangelization">faith and evangelization</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-egsummary_260-0"><a href="#cite_note-egsummary-260">[254]</a></sup> On 8 April 2016, Pope Francis published his second apostolic exhortation, <i><a href="/wiki/Amoris_laetitia" title="Amoris laetitia">Amoris laetitia</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Amoris_laetitia_261-0"><a href="#cite_note-Amoris_laetitia-261">[255]</a></sup> remarking on love within the family. Major controversy erupted at the end of 2016 when four cardinals, supported by some catholic prelates and scholars, asked formally Pope Francis for clarifications, particularly on the issue of giving communion to divorced and civilly remarried Catholics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-262"><a href="#cite_note-262">[256]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-263"><a href="#cite_note-263">[257]</a></sup></p>
<p>He wrote different <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Motu_propio&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Motu propio (page does not exist)">motu propio</a>: <a href="/wiki/Ai_nostri_tempi" title="Ai nostri tempi">Ai nostri tempi</a> and <a href="/wiki/De_concordia_inter_codices" title="De concordia inter codices">De concordia inter codices</a>.</p>
<p>He established two new Secretariats (top-level departments) in the Roman Curia: the <a href="/wiki/Secretariat_for_the_Economy" title="Secretariat for the Economy">Secretariat for the Economy</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Secretariat_for_Communications" title="Secretariat for Communications">Secretariat for Communications</a>. He <a href="/wiki/Matrimonial_nullity_trial_reforms_of_Pope_Francis" title="Matrimonial nullity trial reforms of Pope Francis">reformed</a> the process for declaring <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annulment_(Catholic_Church)" title="Annulment (Catholic Church)">matrimonial nullity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trials_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-trials-264">[258]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Clerical_titles">Clerical titles</span></h3>
<p>In January 2014, Pope Francis said that he would appoint fewer <a href="/wiki/Monsignor" title="Monsignor">monsignors</a> and only assign those honored to the lowest of the three surviving ranks of monsignor, <a href="/wiki/Chaplain_of_His_Holiness" title="Chaplain of His Holiness">Chaplain of His Holiness</a>. It would be awarded only to <a href="/wiki/Diocesan_priest" title="Diocesan priest">diocesan priests</a> at least 65 years old. During his 15 years as Archbishop of Buenos Aires, Pope Francis never sought the title for any of his priests. It is believed he associates it with clerical careerism and hierarchy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[259]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Canonizations_and_beatifications">Canonizations and beatifications</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/List_of_saints_canonized_by_Pope_Francis" title="List of saints canonized by Pope Francis">List of saints canonized by Pope Francis</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_beatified_by_Pope_Francis" title="List of people beatified by Pope Francis">List of people beatified by Pope Francis</a></div>
<p>Pope Francis presided over the first canonizations of his pontificate on 12 May 2013 in which he canonized Antonio Primaldo and his 812 companions as well as the nuns Laura of Saint Catherine of Siena and Maria Guadalupe Garcia Zavalia – in this first canonization he surpassed the record of Pope John Paul II in canonizing the most saints in a pontificate. Francis approved the equipollent canonization of <a href="/wiki/Angela_of_Foligno" title="Angela of Foligno">Angela of Foligno</a> the following 9 October and then the Jesuit <a href="/wiki/Peter_Faber" title="Peter Faber">Peter Faber</a> the following 17 December.</p>
<p>The pope approved further equipollent canonizations on 3 April 2014 for the Jesuit <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_de_Anchieta" title="José de Anchieta">José de Anchieta</a> as well as the <a href="/wiki/Ursulines" title="Ursulines">Ursuline</a> nun <a href="/wiki/Marie_of_the_Incarnation_(Ursuline)" title="Marie of the Incarnation (Ursuline)">Marie of the Incarnation</a> and bishop <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Laval" title="François de Laval">François de Laval</a>. Francis canonized his two predecessors John XXIII and John Paul II on 27 April 2014 and canonized six additional saints the following 23 November. The pope canonized <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Vaz" title="Joseph Vaz">Joseph Vaz</a> on his visit to Sri Lanka on 14 January 2015 and canonized a further four saints on the following 17 May; he canonized Junípero Serra on 23 September while visiting the United States and then canonized four saints on 18 October including the first married couple to be named as saints. Francis canonized <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elisabeth_Hesselblad" title="Elisabeth Hesselblad">Maria Elisabeth Hesselblad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stanislaus_Papczy%C5%84ski" title="Stanislaus Papczyński">Stanislaus Papczyński</a> on 5 June 2016 and then canonized <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teresa_of_Calcutta" title="Teresa of Calcutta">Teresa of Calcutta</a> on 4 September; he canonized seven additional saints on 16 October.</p>
<p>The pope has also continued the practice of having beatifications celebrated in the place of the individual's origin though has presided over beatifications himself on two occasions for <a href="/wiki/Korean_Martyrs" title="Korean Martyrs">Paul Yun Ji-Chung and 123 companions</a> on 16 August 2014 and his predecessor Pope Paul VI on 19 October 2014. The pope has approved beatifications for a range of men and women including the likes of <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_del_Portillo" title="Álvaro del Portillo">Álvaro del Portillo</a> of Opus Dei (27 September 2014) and the martyred archbishop <a href="/wiki/%C3%93scar_Romero" title="Óscar Romero">Óscar Romero</a> (23 May 2015).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consistories">Consistories</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cardinals_created_by_Francis" title="Cardinals created by Francis">Cardinals created by Francis</a></div>
<p>At the first <a href="/wiki/Papal_consistory" title="Papal consistory">consistory</a> of his papacy, held on 22 February 2014, Francis created 19 new cardinals. At the time of their elevation to that rank, 16 of these new cardinals were under eighty years of age and thus eligible to vote in a <a href="/wiki/Papal_conclave" title="Papal conclave">papal conclave</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-266"><a href="#cite_note-266">[260]</a></sup> The new appointees included prelates from South America, Africa, and Asia, including appointees in some of the world's poorest countries, such as <a href="/wiki/Chibly_Langlois" title="Chibly Langlois">Chibly Langlois</a> from <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">Haiti</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippe_Ou%C3%A9draogo_(bishop)" title="Philippe Ouédraogo (bishop)">Philippe Nakellentuba Ouedraogo</a> from <a href="/wiki/Burkina_Faso" title="Burkina Faso">Burkina Faso</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters_267-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-267">[261]</a></sup> The consistory was a rare occasion in which Francis and his predecessor, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benedict_XVI" title="Benedict XVI">Benedict XVI</a>, appeared together in public.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reuters_267-1"><a href="#cite_note-Reuters-267">[261]</a></sup></p>
<p>Benedict XVI also attended the second consistory on 14 February 2015, at which Francis elevated 20 new cardinals, with 15 under the age of eighty and five over the age of eighty. The pope continued his practice of appointing cardinals from the peripheries, such as <a href="/wiki/Charles_Maung_Bo" title="Charles Maung Bo">Charles Maung Bo</a> of <a href="/wiki/Myanmar" title="Myanmar">Myanmar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Soane_Patita_Paini_Mafi" title="Soane Patita Paini Mafi">Soane Patita Paini Mafi</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tonga" title="Tonga">Tonga</a>.</p>
<p>Francis presided over the third consistory of his papacy on 19 November 2016, elevating 17 new cardinals. Of that total number at the time of their elevation, 13 were under the age of eighty and four were over the age of eighty. Francis continued his previous practice of elevating cardinals from the peripheries with an emphasis again on Asia and Africa, such as <a href="/wiki/Patrick_D%27Rozario" title="Patrick D'Rozario">Patrick D'Rozario</a> from <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dieudonn%C3%A9_Nzapalainga" title="Dieudonné Nzapalainga">Dieudonné Nzapalainga</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">Central African Republic</a>, while also naming the first three American cardinals of his papacy and only one Curial appointment.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Year_of_Mercy">Year of Mercy</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Extraordinary_Jubilee_of_Mercy" title="Extraordinary Jubilee of Mercy">Extraordinary Jubilee of Mercy</a></div>
<p>With his April 2015 <a href="/wiki/Papal_bull" title="Papal bull">papal bull</a> of indiction, <i>Misericordiae Vultus</i> (<a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>: "The Face of <a href="/wiki/Mercy" title="Mercy">Mercy</a>"), Francis inaugurated a Special <a href="/wiki/Jubilee_(Christianity)" title="Jubilee (Christianity)">Jubilee Year</a> of Mercy, to run from 8 December 2015, <a href="/wiki/Solemnity" title="Solemnity">Solemnity</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Immaculate_Conception" title="Immaculate Conception">Immaculate Conception</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blessed_Virgin_Mary" title="Blessed Virgin Mary">Blessed Virgin Mary</a>, to the last Sunday before <a href="/wiki/Advent" title="Advent">Advent</a> and the Solemnity of the <a href="/wiki/Feast_of_Christ_the_King" title="Feast of Christ the King">Feast of Christ the King</a> of the Universe on 20 November 2016.</p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holy_Door" title="Holy Door">Holy Doors</a> of the major basilicas of Rome (including the Great Door of St. Peter's) were opened, and special "Doors of Mercy" were opened at cathedrals and other major churches around the world, where the faithful can earn indulgences by fulfilling the usual conditions of prayer for the Pope's intentions, confession, and detachment from sin, and communion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-opening_268-0"><a href="#cite_note-opening-268">[262]</a></sup> During Lent of that year, special 24-hour penance services will be celebrated, and during the year, special qualified and experienced priests called "Missionaries of Mercy" will be available in every diocese to forgive even severe, special-case sins normally reserved to the Holy See's <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_Penitentiary" title="Apostolic Penitentiary">Apostolic Penitentiary</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Misericordiae_269-0"><a href="#cite_note-Misericordiae-269">[263]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-time_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-time-270">[264]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Teachings">Teachings</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Theology_of_Pope_Francis" title="Theology of Pope Francis">Theology of Pope Francis</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Canonization_2014-_The_Canonization_of_Saint_John_XXIII_and_Saint_John_Paul_II_(14036966125).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2746" data-file-width="2913" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Canonization_2014-_The_Canonization_of_Saint_John_XXIII_and_Saint_John_Paul_II_%2814036966125%29.jpg/200px-Canonization_2014-_The_Canonization_of_Saint_John_XXIII_and_Saint_John_Paul_II_%2814036966125%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Canonization_2014-_The_Canonization_of_Saint_John_XXIII_and_Saint_John_Paul_II_%2814036966125%29.jpg/300px-Canonization_2014-_The_Canonization_of_Saint_John_XXIII_and_Saint_John_Paul_II_%2814036966125%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Canonization_2014-_The_Canonization_of_Saint_John_XXIII_and_Saint_John_Paul_II_%2814036966125%29.jpg/400px-Canonization_2014-_The_Canonization_of_Saint_John_XXIII_and_Saint_John_Paul_II_%2814036966125%29.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Canonization_2014-_The_Canonization_of_Saint_John_XXIII_and_Saint_John_Paul_II_(14036966125).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Francis during the canonization of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_XXIII" title="John XXIII">John XXIII</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Paul_II" title="John Paul II">John Paul II</a> on 27 April 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Francis told <a href="/wiki/La_Civilt%C3%A0_Cattolica" title="La Civiltà Cattolica">La Civiltà Cattolica</a> that the church does not need to speak constantly of the issues of abortion, artificial <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contraception" title="Contraception">contraception</a>, and homosexuality. He thought that other issues, notably the duty to help those who are poor and marginalized, have been neglected. He added that the church had focused in trivial issues, and as such should not be so prone to condemn, and that priests should be more welcoming. He said the <a href="/wiki/Confessional" title="Confessional">confessional</a> should be used to motivate people to better themselves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Goodstein_271-0"><a href="#cite_note-Goodstein-271">[265]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC19thSept_272-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBC19thSept-272">[266]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[267]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[268]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mercy">Mercy</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Mercy#Christianity" title="Mercy">Mercy § Christianity</a></div>
<p>Pope Francis said that the most powerful message of Jesus Christ is mercy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vatican.va_275-0"><a href="#cite_note-vatican.va-275">[269]</a></sup> His motto, <i>Miserando atque eligendo</i>, is about Jesus' mercy towards sinners. The phrase is taken from a homily of St. Bede, who commented that Jesus "saw <a href="/wiki/Matthew_the_Apostle" title="Matthew the Apostle">the tax collector</a> and, because he saw him <i>through the eyes of mercy and chose him</i>, he said to him: 'Follow me<span style="padding-right:.2em;">'</span>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[g]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Catholic_News_Service_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-Catholic_News_Service-54">[51]</a></sup> The motto is a reference to the moment when he found his vocation to the priesthood, at the age of 17. He started a day of student celebrations by going to confession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-viewonline.fromdoppler.com_277-0"><a href="#cite_note-viewonline.fromdoppler.com-277">[270]</a></sup></p>
<p>As cardinal he thought Christian morality is not a titanic effort of the will, but a response to the mercy of God. It is not a matter of never falling down but of always getting up again. In this sense, he says Christian morality is a revolution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[271]</a></sup> The Gospel reading for the Sunday he was scheduled to give his first public address as pope was on Jesus' <a href="/wiki/Jesus_and_the_woman_taken_in_adultery" title="Jesus and the woman taken in adultery">forgiveness of the adulterous woman</a>. This allowed him to discuss the principle that God never wearies of forgiving humans and to stress the importance of never tiring in asking for forgiveness.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-279"><a href="#cite_note-279">[272]</a></sup> Because of this emphasis, many have returned to God and to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sacrament_of_Penance_%26_Reconciliation_(Catholic_Church)" title="Sacrament of Penance &amp; Reconciliation (Catholic Church)">confession</a>, a result which has been called the "Francis effect".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[273]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[274]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2015, Pope Francis announced that the universal church would celebrate a Jubilee Year from 8 December 2015 to 20 November 2016, dedicated to the theme of God's mercy. The Vatican announced the pope would perform several acts to demonstrate the theme of God's mercy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282">[275]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Faith_and_evangelization">Faith and evangelization</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Evangelism" title="Evangelism">Evangelism</a></div>
<p>Pope Francis' first encyclical, "<i>Lumen Fidei</i>", was on faith and his first apostolic exhortation, "<i>Evangelii Gaudium</i>", was on the new evangelization. In both his first <a href="/wiki/Homily" title="Homily">homily</a> as pope and in his first address to the cardinals, Francis talked about walking in the presence of Jesus Christ and stressed the church's mission to announce him. In the audience with the cardinals, he emphasized the concept of "encounter with Jesus":</p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Stimulated by the Year of Faith, all together, pastors and faithful, we will make an effort to respond faithfully to the eternal mission: to bring Jesus Christ to humanity, and to lead humanity to an encounter with Jesus Christ: the Way, the Truth, and the Life, truly present in the Church and, at the same time, in every person. This encounter makes us become new men in the mystery of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Actual_grace" title="Actual grace">Grace</a>, provoking in our hearts the Christian joy that is a hundredfold that given us by Christ to those who welcome Him into their lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greets_283-0"><a href="#cite_note-Greets-283">[276]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In his homily, he stressed that "if we do not profess Jesus Christ, things go wrong. We may become a charitable <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">NGO</a>, but not the Church, the <a href="/wiki/Bride_of_Christ" title="Bride of Christ">Bride of the Lord</a>." He went on to teach that "When we do not profess Jesus Christ, we profess the worldliness of the devil... when we profess Christ without the Cross, we are not disciples of the Lord, we are worldly".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284">[277]</a></sup> The theme of rejecting "spiritual worldliness", described as a <i><a href="/wiki/Leitmotif" title="Leitmotif">leitmotif</a></i> of his teachings even before he became pope,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[278]</a></sup> was emphasized in his first apostolic exhortation. Understanding this worldliness as "putting oneself at the center", he said that it is the "greatest danger for the Church, for us, who are in the Church".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[279]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
<div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_0" style="width:220px;" videopayload="&lt;div class=&quot;mediaContainer&quot; style=&quot;width:640px&quot;&gt;&lt;video id=&quot;mwe_player_1&quot; poster=&quot;//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/%E2%96%B6_John_Zizioulas_presents_the_encyclical_Laudato_si%27_at_the_press_conference_in_Rome.webm/640px--%E2%96%B6_John_Zizioulas_presents_the_encyclical_Laudato_si%27_at_the_press_conference_in_Rome.webm.jpg&quot;
