<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%E2%96%B6_John_Zizioulas_presents_the_encyclical_Laudato_si%27_at_the_press_conference_in_Rome.webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/John_Zizioulas" title="John Zizioulas">John Zizioulas</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodoxy" title="Eastern Orthodoxy">Eastern Orthodox</a> <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_bishop" title="Metropolitan bishop">metropolitan</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bergama" title="Bergama">Pergamon</a>, presents the encyclical <i>Laudato si<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span></i> at the <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikibooks.org/wiki/Development_Cooperation_Handbook/Interviews/Press_Conference_Presentation_Laudato_si%27" title="b:Development Cooperation Handbook/Interviews/Press Conference Presentation Laudato si'">Press conference</a> in Rome.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Christian_views_on_environmentalism" title="Christian views on environmentalism">Christian views on environmentalism</a></div>
<p>After his election Francis stated, "Here too, it helps me to think of the name of Francis [of Assisi], who teaches us profound respect for the whole of creation and the protection of our <a href="/wiki/Natural_environment" title="Natural environment">environment</a>, which all too often, instead of using for the good, we exploit greedily, to one another's detriment.".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-287"><a href="#cite_note-287">[280]</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Molise" title="University of Molise">University of Molise</a> he described <a href="/wiki/Environmental_quality" title="Environmental quality">environmental</a> concerns as a great contemporary challenge and voiced opposition to <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">deforestation</a>. He believes that development should respect what Christians see as creation, and that exploiting the earth is sinful.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[281]</a></sup> Francis told the Second International Conference on Nutrition, held in Rome by the <a href="/wiki/Food_and_Agriculture_Organization" title="Food and Agriculture Organization">Food and Agriculture Organization</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289">[282]</a></sup> that a lack of protection for the ecology may generate problems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[283]</a></sup> Francis plans a meeting with leaders of main religions to increase awareness of the state of the climate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-291"><a href="#cite_note-291">[284]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 18 June 2015, Pope Francis issued a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papal_encyclical" title="Papal encyclical">papal encyclical</a> called <i><a href="/wiki/Laudato_si%27" title="Laudato si'">Laudato si'</a></i> on <a href="/wiki/Climate_change" title="Climate change">climate change</a>, care for the environment, and sustainable development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jim_Yardley_and_Laurie_Goodstein_258-1"><a href="#cite_note-Jim_Yardley_and_Laurie_Goodstein-258">[252]</a></sup> The encyclical, although dated 24 May 2015,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-292"><a href="#cite_note-292">[285]</a></sup> was officially made public on 18 June 2015. The encyclical sets apart the basic human needs and appetites. Francis considers that the former are small and non-negotiable, and that the latter are potentially unlimited. Although he asks for the use of <a href="/wiki/Renewable_energy" title="Renewable energy">renewable energy</a> instead of conventional fuels, he thinks that it would not be enough unless society turns down the unlimited appetites of consumerism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293">[286]</a></sup> This project was opposed by Vatican conservatives, Catholic conservatives, and the US evangelical movement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-climate_294-0"><a href="#cite_note-climate-294">[287]</a></sup> In the encyclical, Frances states "The Earth, our home, is beginning to look like an immense pile of filth."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295">[288]</a></sup></p>
<p>As he prepared for the encyclical, Francis sponsored a <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Pontifical Academy of Sciences">Pontifical Academy of Sciences</a> summit meeting in April 2015 that focused on the relationships connecting poverty, economic development, and climate change. The meeting included presentations and discussions by scientists, religious leaders, and economists. The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> secretary general, <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a>, who is urging world leaders to approve a climate-change accord in Paris at the <a href="/wiki/2015_United_Nations_Climate_Change_Conference" title="2015 United Nations Climate Change Conference">2015 United Nations Climate Change Conference</a> in December, delivered the keynote address.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-296"><a href="#cite_note-296">[289]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Poverty">Poverty</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pope_Francis_at_Vargihna.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="532" data-file-width="800" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Pope_Francis_at_Vargihna.jpg/220px-Pope_Francis_at_Vargihna.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Pope_Francis_at_Vargihna.jpg/330px-Pope_Francis_at_Vargihna.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a1/Pope_Francis_at_Vargihna.jpg/440px-Pope_Francis_at_Vargihna.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Pope_Francis_at_Vargihna.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pope Francis visits a <a href="/wiki/Favela" title="Favela">favela</a> in Brazil during the <a href="/wiki/World_Youth_Day_2013" title="World Youth Day 2013">World Youth Day 2013</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Christian_views_on_poverty_and_wealth" title="Christian views on poverty and wealth">Christian views on poverty and wealth</a></div>
<p>At a meeting of Latin American bishops in 2007, Bergoglio said that, despite the economic growth, poverty had not been reduced in the continent, and asked for a better <a href="/wiki/Income_distribution" title="Income distribution">income distribution</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllenPap_297-0"><a href="#cite_note-AllenPap-297">[290]</a></sup> On 30 September 2009, Bergoglio spoke at a conference organized by the <a href="/wiki/Universidad_del_Salvador" title="Universidad del Salvador">Argentina City Postgraduate School (EPOCA)</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Alvear_Palace_Hotel" title="Alvear Palace Hotel">Alvear Palace Hotel</a> in which he quoted the 1992 "Documento de Santo Domingo"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-298"><a href="#cite_note-298">[291]</a></sup> by the <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_Episcopal_Conference" title="Latin American Episcopal Conference">Latin American Episcopal Conference</a>, saying "<a href="/wiki/Extreme_poverty" title="Extreme poverty">extreme poverty</a> and unjust economic structures that cause great <a href="/wiki/Economic_inequality" title="Economic inequality">inequalities</a>" are violations of <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299"><a href="#cite_note-299">[292]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[293]</a></sup> He went on to describe social debt as "immoral, unjust, and illegitimate".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301">[294]</a></sup></p>
<p>During a 48-hour public servant strike in Buenos Aires, Argentina, Bergoglio criticized unequal treatment of the judiciary to poor and rich people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302">[295]</a></sup> In 2002, during <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%932002_Argentine_great_depression" title="1998–2002 Argentine great depression">an economic crisis</a>, Bergoglio harshly criticized those in power, saying, "[l]et's not tolerate the sad spectacle of those who no longer know how to lie and contradict themselves to hold onto their privileges, their rapaciousness, and their ill-earned wealth".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303">[296]</a></sup> During a May 2010 Mass celebrated by twenty bishops commemorating the <a href="/wiki/Argentina_Bicentennial" title="Argentina Bicentennial">Argentina Bicentennial</a> in front of the <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Our_Lady_of_Luj%C3%A1n" title="Basilica of Our Lady of Luján">basilica of Luján</a>, an important Catholic institution and destination of pilgrimage, Bergoglio criticized the reduced social concern over poverty and exhorted Catholics to ask the <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Luj%C3%A1n" title="Our Lady of Luján">Virgin of Luján</a> to "take care of our motherland, particularly those who are most forgotten".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304">[297]</a></sup> In line with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_and_AIDS" title="Catholic Church and AIDS">Catholic Church's efforts to care for AIDS victims</a>, in 2001 he visited a hospice where he washed and kissed the feet of twelve AIDS patients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllenPap_297-1"><a href="#cite_note-AllenPap-297">[290]</a></sup> As Pope Francis he spoke out over the <a href="/wiki/2013_Savar_building_collapse#Worldwide_criticism" title="2013 Savar building collapse">collapse of <i>Rana Plaza</i> garment factory</a> in April 2013, which killed over a thousand people, and condemned the low pay workers received.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305">[298]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pope Francis urged world leaders to prevent excessive monetary ambitions, which he said had become similar to an <a href="/wiki/Idolatry" title="Idolatry">idolatry</a> of money, and urged them to provide more welfare aid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-306"><a href="#cite_note-306">[299]</a></sup> Dealing with the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a>, the pope criticized unbridled capitalism, considering that it judged human beings purely by their ability to consume goods and made people miserable.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307">[300]</a></sup> He said that social inequality is caused by <a href="/wiki/Economic_liberalism" title="Economic liberalism">economic liberalism</a>, and preferred economic systems with a higher intervention by the state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LizzyDavies_308-0"><a href="#cite_note-LizzyDavies-308">[301]</a></sup> During a May 2014 meeting with U.N. Secretary General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a>, Francis called on the United Nations to encourage a better income distribution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309">[302]</a></sup> In 2015, he declared that the poor and downtrodden of the world should have "sacred rights" of labor, lodging, and land, and denounced the <a href="/wiki/Austerity" title="Austerity">austerity</a> imposed by global financial institutions, referring to it as the "new colonialism".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310"><a href="#cite_note-310">[303]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pope Francis deplores <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_slavery" title="Modern slavery">modern slavery</a> and, together with a diverse group of leaders from other religions, he signed a declaration promising to inspire action worldwide in an effort to eliminate slavery by 2020. Both Pope Francis and the declaration described slavery as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crime_against_humanity" title="Crime against humanity">crime against humanity</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311">[304]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-312"><a href="#cite_note-312">[305]</a></sup> During his new year mass in 2015 Francis pressed people from all cultures and religions to combat human trafficking and modern slavery according to their responsibilities. Francis said all human beings are brothers and sisters and all have a right to be free.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-313"><a href="#cite_note-313">[306]</a></sup></p>
<p>Chancellor of Germany <a href="/wiki/Angela_Merkel" title="Angela Merkel">Angela Merkel</a> consulted Francis on 18 May 2013, and later the same day called for more stringent controls of <a href="/wiki/Financial_market" title="Financial market">financial markets</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-huffingtonpost.com_314-0"><a href="#cite_note-huffingtonpost.com-314">[307]</a></sup> Francis has referred many times to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eurozone_crisis" title="Eurozone crisis">Eurozone crisis</a> that affect <a href="/wiki/Greek_government-debt_crisis" title="Greek government-debt crisis">Greece</a> and Roman Catholic Southern European nations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT52513_315-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT52513-315">[308]</a></sup> Nevertheless, Pope Francis considers that starvation and homeless people are bigger problems than the financial crises.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-huffingtonpost.com_314-1"><a href="#cite_note-huffingtonpost.com-314">[307]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/George_Haley" title="George Haley">George Haley</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Haven_University" title="New Haven University">New Haven University</a> said that Francis thinks that capitalism should reduce income disparity, and proposed that he used the diplomatic influence of the Vatican to suggest changes in national economies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnbc.com_316-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnbc.com-316">[309]</a></sup> Rohit Arora is concerned that Francis has not come up with any specific way to solve income inequality and believes if the pope is serious he should do so. Joseph Pastore believes the wealth of the Catholic Church prevents Francis from taking a polarizing position and is unsure how far Francis can reform the Church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnbc.com_316-1"><a href="#cite_note-cnbc.com-316">[309]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pope Francis denounced the "autonomy of the marketplace" and "financial speculation" as tyranny in his 84-page <a href="/wiki/Apostolic_exhortation" title="Apostolic exhortation">apostolic exhortation</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Evangelii_gaudium" title="Evangelii gaudium">Evangelii gaudium</a>:</i></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Just as the commandment "Thou shalt not kill" sets a clear limit in order to safeguard the value of human life, today we also have to say "thou shalt not" to an economy of exclusion and inequality. Such an economy kills. ... A new tyranny is thus born, invisible and often virtual, which unilaterally and relentlessly imposes its own laws and rules. To all this we can add widespread corruption and self-serving tax evasion, which has taken on worldwide dimensions. The thirst for power and possessions knows no limits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317"><a href="#cite_note-317">[310]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318">[311]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Pope Francis' views were called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marxist" title="Marxist">Marxist</a> by <a href="/wiki/Rush_Limbaugh" title="Rush Limbaugh">Rush Limbaugh</a> and other conservatives as a result of his critique of capitalism with absolute market autonomy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marxno_319-0"><a href="#cite_note-marxno-319">[312]</a></sup> Pope Francis responded that "Marxist ideology is wrong. But I have met many Marxists in my life who are good people, so I don't feel offended … there is nothing in the exhortation that cannot be found in the social doctrine of the church."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-marxno_319-1"><a href="#cite_note-marxno-319">[312]</a></sup> He later postulated that the Communists "stole" the flag of Christianity as "the flag of the poor is Christian. Poverty is at the center of the Gospel."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320"><a href="#cite_note-320">[313]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liberation_theology">Liberation theology</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Liberation_theology" title="Liberation theology">Liberation theology</a></div>
<p>Francis opposed the Marxist versions of liberation theology followed by the "'progressive' group of [Jesuit] theologians living out in base communities".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[314]</a></sup> As he wrote in the preface to a book on the Catholic Church in Latin America, <i>Una apuesta por America Latina</i> (A Commitment to Latin America) by <a href="/wiki/Guzm%C3%A1n_Carriquiry_Lecour" title="Guzmán Carriquiry Lecour">Guzmán Carriquiry Lecour</a>, the proponents of liberation theology were unable to reformulate it after the collapse of Marxism, and it thus became an anachronism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gregg_322-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gregg-322">[315]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Surprises_323-0"><a href="#cite_note-Surprises-323">[316]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-324"><a href="#cite_note-324">[317]</a></sup> His theologian of reference was <a href="/wiki/Juan_Carlos_Scannone" title="Juan Carlos Scannone">Juan Carlos Scannone</a>, a fellow Jesuit who had developed a theology centered on the "religious devotion of the common people".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gregg_322-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gregg-322">[315]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Surprises_323-1"><a href="#cite_note-Surprises-323">[316]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325">[318]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VISITA_PAPA_FRANCISCO_I_(19473235041).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2447" data-file-width="3543" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/VISITA_PAPA_FRANCISCO_I_%2819473235041%29.jpg/220px-VISITA_PAPA_FRANCISCO_I_%2819473235041%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/VISITA_PAPA_FRANCISCO_I_%2819473235041%29.jpg/330px-VISITA_PAPA_FRANCISCO_I_%2819473235041%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/VISITA_PAPA_FRANCISCO_I_%2819473235041%29.jpg/440px-VISITA_PAPA_FRANCISCO_I_%2819473235041%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:VISITA_PAPA_FRANCISCO_I_(19473235041).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Thousands of people welcomed Pope Francis in <a href="/wiki/Guayaquil" title="Guayaquil">Guayaquil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecuador" title="Ecuador">Ecuador</a>, 6 July 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Historian Roberto Bosca at the <a href="/wiki/Austral_University_(Argentina)" title="Austral University (Argentina)">Austral University</a> in Buenos Aires says that Pope Francis supported liberation theology's preferential option for the poor, although "in a nonideological fashion".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gregg_322-2"><a href="#cite_note-Gregg-322">[315]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allen2013_326-0"><a href="#cite_note-Allen2013-326">[319]</a></sup> Before becoming Pope, Cardinal Bergoglio described liberation theology's preferential option for the poor as part of a long Christian tradition rooted in the Gospels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-327"><a href="#cite_note-327">[320]</a></sup> Bergoglio's opposition focused on the <a href="/wiki/Montoneros" title="Montoneros">Montoneros</a>, a terrorist group similar to the European <a href="/wiki/Red_Brigades" title="Red Brigades">Red Brigades</a> that caused nearly 6,000 deaths. Montoneros claimed that they ascribed to liberation theology, and sought support from the Church. Bosca considers that Bergoglio's opposition to the liberation theology "wasn't opposition to liberation theology in itself or the option for the poor", but opposition to the possible official Catholic support to the Montoneros.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allen2013_326-1"><a href="#cite_note-Allen2013-326">[319]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite his caution about elements of liberation theology, Francis met with <a href="/wiki/Gustavo_Guti%C3%A9rrez" title="Gustavo Gutiérrez">Gustavo Gutiérrez</a>, who is usually regarded as its founder. Gutiérrez had co-authored a book with <a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Ludwig_M%C3%BCller" title="Gerhard Ludwig Müller">Gerhard Ludwig Müller</a>, prefect of the <a href="/wiki/Congregation_for_the_Doctrine_of_the_Faith" title="Congregation for the Doctrine of the Faith">Congregation for the Doctrine of the Faith</a>. The Vatican's semiofficial newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/L%27Osservatore_Romano" title="L'Osservatore Romano">L'Osservatore Romano</a></i> said at the time that the liberation theology should not continue to be ignored.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328"><a href="#cite_note-328">[321]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pope Francis' beatification of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_San_Salvador#Archbishops" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of San Salvador">Archbishop of San Salvador</a> <a href="/wiki/%C3%93scar_Romero" title="Óscar Romero">Óscar Romero</a>, who was assassinated in March 1980 as he said mass, as a martyr to the church is seen as Francis' strong support for the poor and those who defend that stance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-329"><a href="#cite_note-329">[322]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abortion">Abortion</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_and_abortion" title="Catholic Church and abortion">Catholic Church and abortion</a></div>
<p>Throughout his papacy, Pope Francis has been a vocal opponent of both the practice and legality of abortion. In May 2013, Francis unexpectedly participated in Italy's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pro-life" title="Pro-life">pro-life</a> march in Rome, asking its participants to protect human life "from the moment of conception".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fivemyths_330-0"><a href="#cite_note-fivemyths-330">[323]</a></sup> Also, as the mostly Catholic country of Ireland was preparing legislation to legalize abortion, Francis sent a message to the Irish asking them to protect the lives of both the unborn and vulnerable people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fivemyths_330-1"><a href="#cite_note-fivemyths-330">[323]</a></sup> Also in May 2013, during a Wednesday audience Francis officially blessed the pro-life march in <a href="/wiki/Szczecin" title="Szczecin">Szczecin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a>, one of Europe's largest pro-life events and, speaking in Italian, encouraged the Poles to defend the unborn. He maintained that human life should be respected all the way from conception to natural death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-331"><a href="#cite_note-331">[324]</a></sup></p>
<p>At a September 2013 meeting with Catholic gynecologists, Francis condemned abortion saying that: "Every child that isn't born, but is unjustly condemned to be aborted, has the face of Jesus Christ, has the face of the Lord."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abortion_332-0"><a href="#cite_note-abortion-332">[325]</a></sup> He advised the gynecologists to invoke the <a href="/wiki/Conscience_clause_(medical)" title="Conscience clause (medical)">conscience clause</a> to refuse to perform abortions, if so requested.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abortion_332-1"><a href="#cite_note-abortion-332">[325]</a></sup></p>
<p>Francis also thought, as a Cardinal, that the church should support those women who carry on with their pregnancy despite being <a href="/wiki/Single_parent" title="Single parent">single parents</a>, rejecting the option to abort. He maintained that, in those cases, priests should not refuse to <a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">baptize</a> those children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-333"><a href="#cite_note-333">[326]</a></sup> Pope Francis baptised the baby of an unmarried couple in the <a href="/wiki/Sistine_Chapel" title="Sistine Chapel">Sistine Chapel</a> during <a href="/wiki/Baptism_of_the_Lord" title="Baptism of the Lord">Baptism of the Lord</a> Mass at the Vatican.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-334"><a href="#cite_note-334">[327]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ordination_of_women">Ordination of women</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_doctrine_on_the_ordination_of_women" title="Catholic Church doctrine on the ordination of women">Catholic Church doctrine on the ordination of women</a></div>
<p>Francis has often spoken about the importance of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Women_in_the_Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Women in the Roman Catholic Church">women in the Roman Catholic Church</a>. He considers that they have a special role in spreading the faith to their children and grandchildren. He also considers that, although the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resurrection_appearances_of_Jesus" title="Resurrection appearances of Jesus">first witnesses</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Resurrection_of_Jesus" title="Resurrection of Jesus">resurrection of Jesus</a> were women, their significance was ignored because, for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish_law" title="Jewish law">Jewish law</a> of the time, only males were <a href="/wiki/Credible_witness" title="Credible witness">credible witnesses</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-335"><a href="#cite_note-335">[328]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-336"><a href="#cite_note-336">[329]</a></sup></p>
<p>Francis has addressed the subject of the <a href="/wiki/Ordination_of_women" title="Ordination of women">ordination of women</a> a number of times.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-337"><a href="#cite_note-337">[330]</a></sup> Francis has ruled out the possibility of female priests, stating that this has been the longtime stance of the Church, and that "<a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">John Paul II</a> made the Church's stance <a href="/wiki/Ordinatio_Sacerdotalis" title="Ordinatio Sacerdotalis">definitive</a>. The door is closed."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-338"><a href="#cite_note-338">[331]</a></sup> Francis ruled out female cardinals in December 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSN16.2F12.2F2013_339-0"><a href="#cite_note-CSN16.2F12.2F2013-339">[332]</a></sup></p>
<p>On the other hand, Francis has been noncommittal about whether women should lead more in administration and pastoral activities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-340"><a href="#cite_note-340">[333]</a></sup></p>
<p>Erin Saiz Hanna of the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Ordination_Conference" title="Women's Ordination Conference">Women's Ordination Conference</a> has accused Francis of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Selective_use_of_evidence" title="Selective use of evidence">selective use of evidence</a>. She mentioned that the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Biblical_Commission" title="Pontifical Biblical Commission">Pontifical Biblical Commission</a> had once concluded that there were no scriptural or theological problems with ordaining women, and cited the attitude of Jesus towards women and their leadership in the <a href="/wiki/Early_Christianity" title="Early Christianity">early church</a>. She also suggested that his rejection to the ordination of women may be at odds with his tolerance of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gay_priests" title="Gay priests">gay priests</a>, mentioned in the same interview.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-341"><a href="#cite_note-341">[334]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Clergy">Clergy</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Saludo_en_el_Vaticano.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2368" data-file-width="3552" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Saludo_en_el_Vaticano.JPG/220px-Saludo_en_el_Vaticano.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Saludo_en_el_Vaticano.JPG/330px-Saludo_en_el_Vaticano.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Saludo_en_el_Vaticano.JPG/440px-Saludo_en_el_Vaticano.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Saludo_en_el_Vaticano.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Bishop Gabriel Barba and Pope Francis</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Francis has criticized the perceived hunger for power of some sectors of the curia, which come at the expense of a proper religious life. He thinks that gossip is a danger to the reputation of people, and that the presence of cliques within organizations is a threat to both the individual and the organization.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-342"><a href="#cite_note-342">[335]</a></sup> Francis thinks that priests should be in contact with the people as much as possible and avoid isolation. He also suggests that priests should encourage people to be optimistic.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-343"><a href="#cite_note-343">[336]</a></sup> He has been supported by Rome bishops, priests, deacons, and seminarians from the English-speaking world who attended the second international conference of the Confraternities of Catholic Clergy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-344"><a href="#cite_note-344">[337]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2013, Pope Francis approved the excommunication of Australian priest Greg Reynolds, the first during Francis' papacy. Reynolds was accused of heresy and sacrilegious treatment of the consecrated host. His public preaching contradicting church teaching was also referenced in the letter of excommunication. A letter sent by the Archbishop of Melbourne, <a href="/wiki/Denis_Hart" title="Denis Hart">Denis Hart</a>, to the priests of his diocese cited Reynolds' support for the ordination of women and "his public celebration of the Eucharist when he did not hold faculties to act publicly as a priest". Reynolds said that his support of <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriage</a> was also a factor, though not mentioned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-345"><a href="#cite_note-345">[338]</a></sup></p>
<p>In response to the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_sexual_abuse_cases" title="Catholic Church sexual abuse cases">Catholic Church sexual abuse cases</a>, Francis created the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Commission_for_the_Protection_of_Minors" title="Pontifical Commission for the Protection of Minors">Pontifical Commission for the Protection of Minors</a>. In the past, priests who committed abuses were removed by bishops, but bishops were rarely held accountable. This tribunal was created to prevent cover-ups of abuse cases; offenders would be dealt with by the <a href="/wiki/Congregation_for_the_Doctrine_of_the_Faith" title="Congregation for the Doctrine of the Faith">Congregation for the Doctrine of the Faith</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-346"><a href="#cite_note-346">[339]</a></sup> Barbara Blaine, president of the organization <a href="/wiki/Survivors_Network_of_those_Abused_by_Priests" title="Survivors Network of those Abused by Priests">Survivors Network of those Abused by Priests</a>, considered that it may not be effective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-347"><a href="#cite_note-347">[340]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Priestly_celibacy">Priestly celibacy</span></h4>
<p>As a cardinal, Bergoglio's views regarding the <a href="/wiki/Clerical_celibacy_(Catholic_Church)" title="Clerical celibacy (Catholic Church)">celibacy of priests</a> were recorded in the book <i><a href="/wiki/On_Heaven_and_Earth" title="On Heaven and Earth">On Heaven and Earth</a></i>, a record of conversations conducted with a Buenos Aires rabbi.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gibson_348-0"><a href="#cite_note-gibson-348">[341]</a></sup> He says that celibacy is a matter of discipline rather than faith, and that tradition and experience would advise to keep it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celibacy_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-celibacy-29">[27]</a></sup> He noted that the Byzantine, Ukrainian, Russian, and Greek Catholic Churches allow married men to be ordained priests, but not bishops.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celibacy_29-2"><a href="#cite_note-celibacy-29">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-349"><a href="#cite_note-349">[h]</a></sup> He said that many of those in Western Catholicism who are pushing for more discussion about the issue do so from a position of pragmatism, based on a loss of manpower.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celibacy_29-3"><a href="#cite_note-celibacy-29">[27]</a></sup> He states that "If, hypothetically, Western Catholicism were to review the issue of celibacy, I think it would do so for cultural reasons (as in the East), not so much as a universal option."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celibacy_29-4"><a href="#cite_note-celibacy-29">[27]</a></sup> He emphasized that, in the meantime, the rule must be strictly adhered to, and any priest who cannot obey it should leave the ministry.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-celibacy_29-5"><a href="#cite_note-celibacy-29">[27]</a></sup> The <i>National Catholic Reporter's</i> Vatican analyst, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_J._Reese" title="Thomas J. Reese">Thomas J. Reese</a>, also a Jesuit, praised Bergoglio's use of conditional language.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gibson_348-1"><a href="#cite_note-gibson-348">[341]</a></sup> He said that phrases like "for the moment" and "for now" are "not the kind of qualifications one normally hears when bishops and cardinals discuss celibacy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gibson_348-2"><a href="#cite_note-gibson-348">[341]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contraception">Contraception</span></h3>
<p>The initial reports that Francis considered that the use of methods intended for contraception with the purpose of preventing disease might be permissible<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-350"><a href="#cite_note-350">[342]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-351"><a href="#cite_note-351">[343]</a></sup> were disputed by others who said he was "unwaveringly orthodox on matters of sexual morality".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-352"><a href="#cite_note-352">[344]</a></sup> Before becoming Pope he opposed the free distribution of contraceptives when it was introduced by the Kirchner government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-353"><a href="#cite_note-353">[345]</a></sup> Francis emphasized that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Contraception" title="Contraception">contraception</a> involves "destruction of the family through the privation of children."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-354"><a href="#cite_note-354">[346]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-355"><a href="#cite_note-355">[347]</a></sup> At the same time, Francis teaches that "responsible parenthood" is important, and suggested that population experts recommend three children in a family, and added that Christians do not need to breed in excess.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-356"><a href="#cite_note-356">[348]</a></sup> Francis encourages <a href="/wiki/Natural_family_planning" title="Natural family planning">natural family planning</a> such as avoiding <a href="/wiki/Sexual_intercourse" title="Sexual intercourse">sexual intercourse</a> when the woman is fertile.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-357"><a href="#cite_note-357">[349]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="LGBT_issues">LGBT issues</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality_and_Roman_Catholicism" title="Homosexuality and Roman Catholicism">Homosexuality and Roman Catholicism</a></div>
<p>As bishop and Pope, Francis restated the <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality_and_Roman_Catholicism" title="Homosexuality and Roman Catholicism">Church's principle</a>: that homosexual practice is intrinsically immoral, but that every homosexual person should be treated with respect and love.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inflight_358-0"><a href="#cite_note-inflight-358">[350]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-359"><a href="#cite_note-359">[351]</a></sup> He opposes <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriage</a>, including the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_Argentina" title="Same-sex marriage in Argentina">bill to introduce it in Argentina</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pentin_360-0"><a href="#cite_note-pentin-360">[352]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cbc20130318_361-0"><a href="#cite_note-cbc20130318-361">[353]</a></sup> In July 2010, while the law was under consideration, he wrote a letter to Argentina's cloistered nuns in which he said the Argentine <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_family" title="Nuclear family">nuclear family</a> could be seriously harmed. He thought that children would face discrimination and lose the development that a father and mother give.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pentin_360-1"><a href="#cite_note-pentin-360">[352]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-feder_362-0"><a href="#cite_note-feder-362">[354]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-363"><a href="#cite_note-363">[355]</a></sup></p>
<blockquote class="templatequote">
<p>Let's not be naïve: This is not a simple political fight; it is a destructive proposal to God's plan. This is not a mere legislative proposal (that's just its form), but a move by the father of lies that seeks to confuse and deceive the children of God ... Let's look to St. Joseph, Mary, and the Child to ask fervently that they defend the Argentine family in this moment... May they support, defend, and accompany us in this war of God.</p>
</blockquote>
<p>After <i><a href="/wiki/L%27Osservatore_Romano" title="L'Osservatore Romano">L'Osservatore Romano</a></i> reported this, several priests expressed their support for the law and one was defrocked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-364"><a href="#cite_note-364">[356]</a></sup> Observers believe that the church's opposition and Bergoglio's language worked in favor of the law's passage and that in response, Catholic officials adopted a more conciliatory tone in later debates on social issues such as parental <a href="/wiki/Surrogacy" title="Surrogacy">surrogacy</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-365"><a href="#cite_note-365">[357]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rubin, Bergoglio's biographer, said that while taking a strong stand against same-sex marriage, Bergoglio raised the possibility in 2010 with his bishops in Argentina that they support the idea of <a href="/wiki/Civil_union" title="Civil union">civil unions</a> as a compromise position.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pragmatist_366-0"><a href="#cite_note-pragmatist-366">[358]</a></sup> According to one news report by <i>The New York Times</i>, a majority of the bishops voted to overrule him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pragmatist_366-1"><a href="#cite_note-pragmatist-366">[358]</a></sup> Miguel Woites, the director of the Catholic News Agency of Argentina, denied that Bergoglio ever made such a proposal,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Catholic_News_Agency_367-0"><a href="#cite_note-Catholic_News_Agency-367">[359]</a></sup> but additional sources, including two Argentine journalists and two senior officials of the Argentine bishops conference, supported Rubin's account.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hardquestions_368-0"><a href="#cite_note-hardquestions-368">[360]</a></sup></p>
<p>In an interview on 28 July 2013, when discussing homosexuals (both in general and their place in the clergy) and answering a question as to whether there was a "gay lobby" in the Vatican, the pontiff said, "If someone is gay and is searching for the Lord and has good will, then who am I to judge him? The Catechism of the Catholic Church explains this in a beautiful way, saying … wait a moment, how does it say it … it says: “no one should marginalize these people for this, they must be integrated into society”."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pope_Full_declerations_369-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pope_Full_declerations-369">[361]</a></sup> According to two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gay_right" title="Gay right">gay rights</a> activists, Marcelo Márquez and Andrés Albertsen, Bergoglio expressed support for the spiritual needs of "homosexual people" and willingness to support "measured actions" on their behalf in private conversations with them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-closed_doors_370-0"><a href="#cite_note-closed_doors-370">[362]</a></sup> These remarks have been seen as an encouraging change of tone from the papacy, so much so that the American <a href="/wiki/LGBT" title="LGBT">LGBT</a> magazine <i><a href="/wiki/The_Advocate" title="The Advocate">The Advocate</a></i> named Pope Francis their Person of the Year for 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-371"><a href="#cite_note-371">[363]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 5 January 2014, the Vatican denied that the Pontiff supports <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gay_union" title="Gay union">gay unions</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-372"><a href="#cite_note-372">[364]</a></sup> In response to various Italian <a href="/wiki/Tabloid_journalism" title="Tabloid journalism">tabloid</a> articles released in the media, Vatican spokesman Father <a href="/wiki/Federico_Lombardi" title="Federico Lombardi">Federico Lombardi</a> cited that various media misinterpretations are "paradoxical" and manipulative in misusing Pope Francis' words noted in response to children growing up in non-traditional families.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes.com_373-0"><a href="#cite_note-latimes.com-373">[365]</a></sup> <i>The New York Times</i> considers that Bergoglio may have supported gay unions in Argentina only as a negotiated compromise, but that his context as a Pope is very different.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pragmatist_366-2"><a href="#cite_note-pragmatist-366">[358]</a></sup> In 2015, Pope Francis declared that "the family is threatened by growing efforts on the part of some to redefine the very institution of marriage" and suggested that same-sex marriage "disfigures God's plan for creation".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ben_Tufft_374-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ben_Tufft-374">[366]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Michele_Richinick_375-0"><a href="#cite_note-Michele_Richinick-375">[367]</a></sup> The Pontiff supported the <a href="/wiki/Slovak_same-sex_marriage_referendum,_2015" title="Slovak same-sex marriage referendum, 2015">Slovak referendum</a> on banning gay marriage and gay adoption in an address to St. Peter's Square, stating: "I wish to express my appreciation to the entire Slovak church, encouraging everyone to continue their efforts in defense of the family, the vital cell of society."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-J_Lester_Feder_376-0"><a href="#cite_note-J_Lester_Feder-376">[368]</a></sup> In October 2015, priest and Vatican theologian Priest <a href="/wiki/Krzysztof_Charamsa" title="Krzysztof Charamsa">Krzysztof Charamsa</a> was stripped of his posts after announcing he was homosexual and denouncing the Church for "persecuting" and causing "immeasurable suffering" to homosexuals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-377"><a href="#cite_note-377">[369]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-378"><a href="#cite_note-378">[370]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 2 October 2016, Pope Francis spoke in favor of pastoral care for and including <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">transgender</a> Catholics in the church, stating priests should "accompany them spiritually" and that they should never be turned away, even if they have undergone <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gender_transition" title="Gender transition">gender transition</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sex_reassignment_surgery" title="Sex reassignment surgery">sex-reassignment operations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-379"><a href="#cite_note-379">[371]</a></sup> He spoke out against "Gender Theory", that is the concept that <a href="/wiki/Gender_identity" title="Gender identity">gender identity</a> is not definite and can change, being taught in schools and referred to it as "ideological colonization" and said it was one of the threats against traditional marriage and is destructive to children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-380"><a href="#cite_note-380">[372]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-381"><a href="#cite_note-381">[373]</a></sup></p>
<p>Francis once held an audience with a Spanish transgender man, who had transitioned from female to male, and his wife.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-382"><a href="#cite_note-382">[374]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/New_Ways_Ministry" title="New Ways Ministry">New Ways Ministry</a> and <a href="/wiki/DignityUSA" title="DignityUSA">DignityUSA</a>, LGBT Catholic Advocacy groups, both spoke out against Pope Francis' statements regarding gender identity, calling it "dangerous ignorance" of the issue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-383"><a href="#cite_note-383">[375]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_persecution">Religious persecution</span></h3>
<p>Francis condemned persecution of religious minorities in <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a> including <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Christians_by_ISIL" title="Persecution of Christians by ISIL">some Christian victims</a>. He did not mention the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant</a> specifically but is believed to have referred to it. Francis mentioned children dying of hunger and thirst, kidnapped women, massacres, and violence of all kinds. In the opinion of Francis war and hatred cannot be carried out in the name of God. Francis thanked brave people bringing aid to those driven from their homes. He confidently expects an effective solution to stop those crimes and return the area to the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-384"><a href="#cite_note-384">[376]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-385"><a href="#cite_note-385">[377]</a></sup> and, in a break with Vatican tradition, supports the use of force to stop Islamic militants from attacking religious minorities in Iraq.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-386"><a href="#cite_note-386">[378]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-387"><a href="#cite_note-387">[379]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-388"><a href="#cite_note-388">[380]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Capital_punishment_and_life_imprisonment">Capital punishment and life imprisonment</span></h3>
<p>Pope Francis proposed the abolition of both <a href="/wiki/Capital_punishment" title="Capital punishment">capital punishment</a> and <a href="/wiki/Life_imprisonment" title="Life imprisonment">life imprisonment</a> in a meeting with representatives of the <a href="/wiki/International_Association_of_Penal_Law" title="International Association of Penal Law">International Association of Penal Law</a>. He thinks that states should find another way to protect people from aggression, and includes deaths caused by <a href="/wiki/Police_brutality" title="Police brutality">police brutality</a> and <a href="/wiki/Extrajudicial_punishment" title="Extrajudicial punishment">extrajudicial punishment</a>. He accepted that the Church accepts it when there are no other options to protect the people, but considers that nowadays such cases may be minimal or even nonexistent. He also thinks that life imprisonment, recently removed from the Vatican penal code, is just a variation of the death penalty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-389"><a href="#cite_note-389">[381]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Role_in_international_diplomacy">Role in international diplomacy</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:President_Barack_Obama_with_Pope_Francis_at_the_Vatican,_March_27,_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/President_Barack_Obama_with_Pope_Francis_at_the_Vatican%2C_March_27%2C_2014.jpg/220px-President_Barack_Obama_with_Pope_Francis_at_the_Vatican%2C_March_27%2C_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/President_Barack_Obama_with_Pope_Francis_at_the_Vatican%2C_March_27%2C_2014.jpg/330px-President_Barack_Obama_with_Pope_Francis_at_the_Vatican%2C_March_27%2C_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/President_Barack_Obama_with_Pope_Francis_at_the_Vatican%2C_March_27%2C_2014.jpg/440px-President_Barack_Obama_with_Pope_Francis_at_the_Vatican%2C_March_27%2C_2014.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:President_Barack_Obama_with_Pope_Francis_at_the_Vatican,_March_27,_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pope Francis with <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">U.S. President</a> <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, 27 March 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_with_Franciscus_(2015-06-10)_1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1160" data-file-width="1880" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Vladimir_Putin_with_Franciscus_%282015-06-10%29_1.jpg/220px-Vladimir_Putin_with_Franciscus_%282015-06-10%29_1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Vladimir_Putin_with_Franciscus_%282015-06-10%29_1.jpg/330px-Vladimir_Putin_with_Franciscus_%282015-06-10%29_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Vladimir_Putin_with_Franciscus_%282015-06-10%29_1.jpg/440px-Vladimir_Putin_with_Franciscus_%282015-06-10%29_1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vladimir_Putin_with_Franciscus_(2015-06-10)_1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pope Francis shaking hands with <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russian</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Foreign_Minister" title="Foreign Minister">Foreign Minister</a> <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Lavrov" title="Sergey Lavrov">Sergey Lavrov</a>, behind <a href="/wiki/President_of_Russia" title="President of Russia">Russian President</a> <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Putin" title="Vladimir Putin">Vladimir Putin</a>, 10 June 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Pope Francis played a key role in the talks toward restoring <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuban_Thaw" title="Cuban Thaw">full diplomatic relations between the U.S. and Cuba</a>. The restoration was jointly announced by U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> and Cuban President <a href="/wiki/Ra%C3%BAl_Castro" title="Raúl Castro">Raúl Castro</a> on Wednesday, 17 December 2014. The headline in the <i>Los Angeles Times</i> on 19 December 2014 was "Bridge to Cuba via Vatican," with the further lead "In a rare and crucial role, Pope Francis helped keep U.S. talks with Havana on track and guided final deal."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-390"><a href="#cite_note-390">[382]</a></sup> The pope was a behind the scenes broker of the agreement, taking the role following <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">President Obama's</a> request during his visit to the pope in March 2014. The success of the negotiations was credited to Francis because "as a religious leader with the confidence of both sides, he was able to convince the Obama and Castro administrations that the other side would live up to the deal".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-391"><a href="#cite_note-391">[383]</a></sup> En route to the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> for a visit in September 2015, the pope stopped in <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">Cuba</a>. "The plan comes amid a breakthrough for which Francis has received much credit."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-392"><a href="#cite_note-392">[384]</a></sup> The Cuba visit "seals that accomplishment, in which he served as a bridge between two erstwhile enemies".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilkinson.2C_Pope_will_visit_Cuba._393-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wilkinson.2C_Pope_will_visit_Cuba.-393">[385]</a></sup> According to one expert on religion in Latin America, Mario Paredes, the pope's visit to Cuba is consistent with his aim to promote an understanding of the role of the Cuban Revolution and that of the Catholic Church. When Francis was archbishop of Buenos Aires he authored a text entitled "Dialogues Between John Paul II and Fidel Castro."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wilkinson.2C_Pope_will_visit_Cuba._393-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wilkinson.2C_Pope_will_visit_Cuba.-393">[385]</a></sup> John Paul was the first pope to visit Cuba. In May 2015, the pope met with Cuban leader Raúl Castro. After the meeting in <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a> on 10 May 2015, Castro said that he is considering returning to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Catholic_Cuba_394-0"><a href="#cite_note-Catholic_Cuba-394">[386]</a></sup> He said in a televised news conference, "I read all the speeches of the pope, his commentaries, and if the pope continues this way, I will go back to praying and go back to the [Roman Catholic] church. I am not joking."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-395"><a href="#cite_note-395">[387]</a></sup> Castro said that when the pope comes, "I promise to go to all his Masses and with satisfaction".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-396"><a href="#cite_note-396">[388]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2014, Pope Francis declined to meet with the <a href="/wiki/14th_Dalai_Lama" title="14th Dalai Lama">14th Dalai Lama</a>, the 1989 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a> laureate. According to a <i>New York Times</i> report, a Vatican spokesman said "Pope Francis obviously holds the Dalai Lama in very high regard, but he will not be meeting any of the Nobel [Peace] laureates."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-397"><a href="#cite_note-397">[389]</a></sup> The last meeting between the Dalai Lama and a pope was with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benedict_XVI" title="Benedict XVI">Benedict XVI</a> in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-398"><a href="#cite_note-398">[390]</a></sup> In November 2015, Pope Francis met with that year's <a href="/wiki/Tunisian_National_Dialogue_Quartet" title="Tunisian National Dialogue Quartet">Nobel Peace Prize laureates from Tunisia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-399"><a href="#cite_note-399">[391]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2014, his visit to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/State_of_Israel" title="State of Israel">state of Israel</a> was heavily publicized. However, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protests_Against_Pope_Francis_Visit_to_Israel_2014" title="Protests Against Pope Francis Visit to Israel 2014">protests against his visit</a> resulted in an alleged arson attempt at the <a href="/wiki/Dormition_Abbey" title="Dormition Abbey">Dormition Abbey</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-400"><a href="#cite_note-400">[392]</a></sup> The cave under the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_the_Nativity" title="Church of the Nativity">Church of the Nativity</a> caught fire the night after his visit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-401"><a href="#cite_note-401">[393]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2015, Pope Francis welcomed Palestinian president <a href="/wiki/Mahmoud_Abbas" title="Mahmoud Abbas">Mahmoud Abbas</a> to the Vatican. Several media outlets reported that Francis praised Abbas as "an angel of peace", though his actual words were the following: "The angel of peace destroys the evil spirit of war. I thought about you: may you be an angel of peace."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-402"><a href="#cite_note-402">[394]</a></sup> The Vatican signed a treaty recognizing the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">state of Palestine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-403"><a href="#cite_note-403">[395]</a></sup> The Vatican issued statements concerning the hope that the peace talks could resume between Israel and Palestine. Abbas' visit was on the occasion of the canonization of two Palestinian nuns.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-404"><a href="#cite_note-404">[396]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 6 June 2015, Pope Francis visited <a href="/wiki/Sarajevo" title="Sarajevo">Sarajevo</a>, the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>. He urged peace during his time in the religiously diverse city, known as the "Jerusalem of Europe".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-405"><a href="#cite_note-405">[397]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 25 September 2015, Pope Francis addressed the United Nations in New York City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Times_2015_406-0"><a href="#cite_note-Times_2015-406">[398]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 16 April 2016, he visited, together with the <a href="/wiki/Bartholomew_I_of_Constantinople" title="Bartholomew I of Constantinople">Ecumenical Patriarch Bartholomew</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ieronymos_II_of_Athens" title="Ieronymos II of Athens">Archbishop Ieronimos II of Athens</a>, the Mòria camp in the <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greek</a> island of <a href="/wiki/Lesbos" title="Lesbos">Lesbos</a>, to call the attention of the world to the refugee issue. There the three Christian leaders signed a joint declaration<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-407"><a href="#cite_note-407">[399]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pope Francis has said he will visit Ireland in 2018, in what will be the first papal tour of the country since John Paul II’s historic trip in 1979.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-408"><a href="#cite_note-408">[400]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_image">Public image</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_places_and_things_named_after_Pope_Francis" title="List of places and things named after Pope Francis">List of places and things named after Pope Francis</a></div>
<p>Popular <a href="/wiki/Mainstream_media" title="Mainstream media">mainstream media</a> frequently portray Pope Francis either as a <a href="/wiki/Progressivism" title="Progressivism">progressive</a> papal reformer or with <a href="/wiki/Social_liberalism" title="Social liberalism">liberal</a>, moderate values.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-409"><a href="#cite_note-409">[401]</a></sup> The Vatican has claimed that Western news outlets often seek to portray his message with a less-doctrinal tone of papacy, in hopes of extrapolating his words to convey a more merciful and tolerant message.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Achanging_410-0"><a href="#cite_note-Achanging-410">[402]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-411"><a href="#cite_note-411">[403]</a></sup> In the news media, both faithful and non-believers often refer to a "honeymoon" phase in which the Pope has changed the tone on Catholic doctrines and supposedly initiated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical" title="Ecclesiastical">ecclesiastical</a> reform in the Vatican.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-412"><a href="#cite_note-412">[404]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-413"><a href="#cite_note-413">[405]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-414"><a href="#cite_note-414">[406]</a></sup> Media systems differ, too, not only in their coverage of Francis's stances but also in how individual events are portrayed. His 2015 trip to Cuba is a prime example. During this trip, American-based AP and British-based Reuters highlighted the religious aspect of the pope’s journey while Prensa Latina, the official state media agency, depicted it as a diplomatic visit. American and British media were also more likely during this trip to show Francis interacting with regular Cubans compared to the official Cuban media, which showed Francis interacting with elites most often.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-415"><a href="#cite_note-415">[407]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2013, both <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Time_Magazine" title="Time Magazine">Time</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Advocate" title="The Advocate">The Advocate</a></i> magazines named the Pontiff as their "Person of the Year" in praise and hopes of reforming the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Curia" title="Roman Curia">Roman Curia</a> while hoping to change the Catholic Church's doctrine on various controversial issues. In addition, <i>Esquire</i> magazine named him as the "Best-dressed man" for 2013 for his simpler vestments often in tune with a modern simplistic design on sartorial fashion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-416"><a href="#cite_note-416">[408]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine followed in January 2014 by making the Pontiff their featured front cover.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-417"><a href="#cite_note-417">[409]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-418"><a href="#cite_note-418">[410]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Fortune_(magazine)" title="Fortune (magazine)">Fortune</a></i> magazine also ranked Pope Francis as number one in their list of 50 greatest leaders.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-419"><a href="#cite_note-419">[411]</a></sup> On 5 November 2014, he was ranked by <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> as the fourth <a href="/wiki/Forbes_list_of_The_World%27s_Most_Powerful_People" title="Forbes list of The World's Most Powerful People">most powerful person in the world</a> and was the only non-political figure in the top ranking.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-420"><a href="#cite_note-420">[412]</a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2013, a new song was dedicated to Francis and released in Brazilian Portuguese, European Portuguese, and Italian, titled <i>Come Puoi</i> ("How You Can").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nofrills_184-1"><a href="#cite_note-nofrills-184">[179]</a></sup> Also in March, Pablo Buera, the mayor of <a href="/wiki/La_Plata" title="La Plata">La Plata</a>, Argentina, announced that the city had renamed a section of a street leading up to a local cathedral <i>Papa Francisco</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-street_421-0"><a href="#cite_note-street-421">[413]</a></sup> There are already efforts to name other streets after him, as well as a school where he studied as a child.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-street_421-1"><a href="#cite_note-street-421">[413]</a></sup> A proposal to create a commemorative coin as a tribute to Pope Francis was made in Argentina's lower house on 28 November 2013. On the coins it would read, "Tribute from the Argentine People to Pope Francis." beneath his face.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-422"><a href="#cite_note-422">[414]</a></sup> As of May 2013, sales of papal souvenirs, a sign of popularity, were up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT52513_315-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT52513-315">[308]</a></sup></p>
<p>Pope Francis presided over his first joint public wedding ceremony in a Nuptial Mass for 20 couples from the Archdiocese of Rome on 14 September 2014, just a few weeks before the start of 5–19 October Extraordinary <a href="/wiki/Synod_of_Bishops_(Catholic)" title="Synod of Bishops (Catholic)">Synod of Bishops</a> on the Family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-423"><a href="#cite_note-423">[415]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-425"><a href="#cite_note-425">[i]</a></sup></p>
<p>To date, there are two biographical films about Pope Francis: <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Call_Me_Francesco" title="Call Me Francesco">Call Me Francesco</a></i> (Italy, 2015), starring <a href="/wiki/Rodrigo_de_la_Serna" title="Rodrigo de la Serna">Rodrigo de la Serna</a>, and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francis:_Pray_for_me" title="Francis: Pray for me">Francis: Pray for me</a></i> (Argentina, 2015), starring <a href="/wiki/Dar%C3%ADo_Grandinetti" title="Darío Grandinetti">Darío Grandinetti</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-426"><a href="#cite_note-426">[417]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2016, while in Mexico, Pope Francis made international headlines for criticizing U.S. <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_presidential_candidates,_2016" title="Republican Party presidential candidates, 2016">Republican presidential candidate</a> <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-427"><a href="#cite_note-427">[418]</a></sup> Francis said of <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, <i>"A person who thinks only about building walls, wherever they may be, and not building bridges, is not Christian. This is not the gospel."</i> Trump responded saying "<i>For a religious leader to question a person’s faith is disgraceful.</i>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-428"><a href="#cite_note-428">[419]</a></sup> Father <a href="/wiki/Federico_Lombardi" title="Federico Lombardi">Federico Lombardi</a> defended the pope remarks saying that they weren't by any means "a personal attack, nor an indication of who to vote for".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-429"><a href="#cite_note-429">[420]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 19 March 2016, Pope Francis became the first Pope to create an <a href="/wiki/Instagram" title="Instagram">Instagram</a> account. He broke records after having gained over one million followers in under twelve hours of the account being up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-430"><a href="#cite_note-430">[421]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 8 January 2017 at a ceremony commemorating the <a href="/wiki/Baptism_of_Jesus" title="Baptism of Jesus">Baptism of Jesus</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Sistine_Chapel" title="Sistine Chapel">Sistine Chapel</a> in which twenty-eight infants were to be baptized, Pope Francis reiterated support for mothers to <a href="/wiki/Breastfeeding_in_public" title="Breastfeeding in public">breastfeed their children in public</a>, even in sacred places.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-431"><a href="#cite_note-431">[422]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-432"><a href="#cite_note-432">[423]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Distinctions">Distinctions</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles_and_styles">Titles and styles</span></h3>
<table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em">
<tr>
<th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-weight: normal; background-color: gold;"><span style="font-size:80%">Papal styles of</span><br/>
<b><span class="fn">Pope Francis</span></b></th>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Insigne_Francisci.svg"><img alt="Insigne Francisci.svg" data-file-height="1120" data-file-width="800" height="84" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Insigne_Francisci.svg/60px-Insigne_Francisci.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Insigne_Francisci.svg/90px-Insigne_Francisci.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Insigne_Francisci.svg/120px-Insigne_Francisci.svg.png 2x" width="60"/></a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Style_(manner_of_address)" title="Style (manner of address)">Reference style</a></th>
<td><a href="/wiki/His_Holiness" title="His Holiness">His Holiness</a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Spoken style</th>
<td>Your Holiness</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Religious style</th>
<td>Holy Father</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The official <a href="/wiki/Style_(manner_of_address)" title="Style (manner of address)">style</a> of the Pope in English is <i>His Holiness Pope Francis</i>; in Latin, <i>Franciscus, Episcopus Romae</i>. <i>Holy Father</i> is another honorific often used for popes.</p>
<p>His full title, rarely used, is:</p>
<dl>
<dd><i><a href="/wiki/His_Holiness" title="His Holiness">His Holiness</a> Francis, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Rome" title="Bishop of Rome">Bishop of Rome</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vicar_of_Christ" title="Vicar of Christ">Vicar of Jesus Christ</a>, Successor of the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter" title="Saint Peter">Prince of the Apostles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pontifex_Maximus" title="Pontifex Maximus">Supreme</a> <a href="/wiki/Pontiff#Christianity" title="Pontiff">Pontiff</a> of the Universal Church, <a href="/wiki/Primate_(bishop)" title="Primate (bishop)">Primate</a> of Italy, <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_bishop" title="Metropolitan bishop">Archbishop and Metropolitan</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_the_Roman_Catholic_dioceses_in_Italy#Ecclesiastical_Province_of_Rome" title="List of the Roman Catholic dioceses in Italy">Roman</a> <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_province#Catholic_Church" title="Ecclesiastical province">Province</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Sovereigns_of_the_Vatican_City_State" title="List of Sovereigns of the Vatican City State">Sovereign</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a> State, <a href="/wiki/Servant_of_the_servants_of_God" title="Servant of the servants of God">Servant of the servants of God</a>.</i></dd>
</dl>
<p>The best-known title, that of "Pope", does not appear in the official list of titles, but is commonly used in the titles of documents, and appears, in abbreviated form, in their signatures as "PP." standing for <i>Papa</i> (<i>Pope</i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-433"><a href="#cite_note-433">[424]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-434"><a href="#cite_note-434">[425]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-435"><a href="#cite_note-435">[426]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-436"><a href="#cite_note-436">[427]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-437"><a href="#cite_note-437">[428]</a></sup></p>
<p>It is customary when referring to popes to translate the <a href="/wiki/Regnal_name" title="Regnal name">regnal name</a> into local languages. Thus he is <i>Papa Franciscus</i> in Latin (the official language of the Holy See), <i>Papa Francesco</i> in Italian (the language of the Vatican), <i>Papa Francisco</i> in his native Spanish, and <i>Pope Francis</i> in English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-438"><a href="#cite_note-438">[429]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="National_orders">National orders</span></h3>
<p>As <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Pope</a>, representative of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> of <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">Vatican City</a>, Francis is <a href="/wiki/Grand_Master_(order)" title="Grand Master (order)">Grand Master</a> of the following orders:</p>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/15px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/30px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png 2x" width="15"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>: <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Order_of_Christ" title="Supreme Order of Christ">Supreme Order of Christ</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/15px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/30px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png 2x" width="15"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>: <a href="/wiki/Order_of_the_Golden_Spur" title="Order of the Golden Spur">Order of the Golden Spur</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/15px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/30px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png 2x" width="15"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Order_of_Pius_IX" title="Order of Pius IX">Order of Pius IX</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/15px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/30px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png 2x" width="15"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>: <a href="/wiki/Order_of_St._Gregory_the_Great" title="Order of St. Gregory the Great">Order of St. Gregory the Great</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="500" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/15px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg/30px-Flag_of_the_Vatican_City.svg.png 2x" width="15"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a>: <a href="/wiki/Order_of_St._Sylvester" title="Order of St. Sylvester">Order of St. Sylvester</a></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_orders">Foreign orders</span></h3>
<ul>

<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="750" data-file-width="1100" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Flag_of_Bolivia.svg/22px-Flag_of_Bolivia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Flag_of_Bolivia.svg/34px-Flag_of_Bolivia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Flag_of_Bolivia.svg/44px-Flag_of_Bolivia.svg.png 2x" width="22"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Bolivia" title="Bolivia">Bolivia</a>: Order of Merit "Father Luis Espinal Camps" (9 July 2015) <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CondorDeLosAndes_439-1"><a href="#cite_note-CondorDeLosAndes-439">[430]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CrucifixThis_440-1"><a href="#cite_note-CrucifixThis-440">[431]</a></sup></li>

</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards">Awards</span></h3>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1000" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/23px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/35px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Germany.svg/46px-Flag_of_Germany.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>: <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne_Prize" title="Charlemagne Prize">International Charlemagne Prize</a> of <a href="/wiki/Aachen" title="Aachen">Aachen</a> 2016</li>
<li>"Person of the Year" by <a href="/wiki/People_for_the_Ethical_Treatment_of_Animals" title="People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals">People for the Ethical Treatment of Animals</a> (2015) for his request that all Catholics be kind to animals<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-442"><a href="#cite_note-442">[433]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
