</div>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="900" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_Philippines.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>: The Pope Francis Center for the Poor – <a href="/wiki/Palo,_Leyte" title="Palo, Leyte">Palo, Leyte</a> (12 July 2015)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-444"><a href="#cite_note-444">[435]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ennio_Morricone" title="Ennio Morricone">Ennio Morricone</a> composed a Mass setting (<i>Missa Papae Francisci</i>) named after the Pope, for the occasion of the 200th anniversary of the restoration of the Jesuit order. The performance aired on <a href="/wiki/Rai_5" title="Rai 5">Rai 5</a> and was attended by former Italian President <a href="/wiki/Giorgio_Napolitano" title="Giorgio Napolitano">Giorgio Napolitano</a> and other dignitaries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-445"><a href="#cite_note-445">[436]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-446"><a href="#cite_note-446">[437]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-447"><a href="#cite_note-447">[438]</a></sup></li>
<li>The composer <a href="/wiki/Ludger_St%C3%BChlmeyer" title="Ludger Stühlmeyer">Ludger Stühlmeyer</a> dedicated his work <i>Klangrede – Sonnengesang des <a href="/wiki/Francis_of_Assisi" title="Francis of Assisi">Franziskus</a></i>, for choir (SATB) and instruments, to Pope Francis (<i>Suae Sanctitati Papae Francisci dedicat.</i>). First performance: Capella Mariana 4 October 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-448"><a href="#cite_note-448">[439]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Appreciation">Appreciation</span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Oratorio" title="Oratorio">oratorio</a> <a href="/wiki/Laudato_si%27_(oratorio)" title="Laudato si' (oratorio)">Laudato si'</a> by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Reulein" title="Peter Reulein">Peter Reulein</a> (music) written on a <a href="/wiki/Libretto" title="Libretto">libretto</a> by <a href="/wiki/Helmut_Schlegel" title="Helmut Schlegel">Helmut Schlegel</a> <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Friars_Minor" title="Order of Friars Minor">OFM</a>, the figure of Pope Francis appears next to <a href="/wiki/Mary,_mother_of_Jesus" title="Mary, mother of Jesus">Mary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francis_of_Assisi" title="Francis of Assisi">Francis of Assisi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Clare_of_Assisi" title="Clare of Assisi">Clare of Assisi</a>. In the oratorio, Pope Franziskus suggests a bridge from the crucifixion scene on <a href="/wiki/Calvary" title="Calvary">Golgotha</a> to the suffering of the present. He emphasizes the female talent and the importance of the charism of women for church and society. The texts of the <a href="/wiki/Encyclical" title="Encyclical">encyclical</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Laudato_si%27" title="Laudato si'">Laudato si'</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Evangelii_gaudium" title="Evangelii gaudium">Evangelii gaudium</a></i> were used. The motto of the <a href="/wiki/Extraordinary_Jubilee_of_Mercy" title="Extraordinary Jubilee of Mercy">Extraordinary Jubilee of Mercy</a> also plays a central role.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Laudato_si-score_449-0"><a href="#cite_note-Laudato_si-score-449">[440]</a></sup> The oratorio was premiered on 6 November 2016 in the <a href="/wiki/Limburg_Cathedral" title="Limburg Cathedral">Limburg Cathedral</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Laudato_si-Liebfrauen_450-0"><a href="#cite_note-Laudato_si-Liebfrauen-450">[441]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Coat_of_arms">Coat of arms</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_Pope_Francis" title="Coat of arms of Pope Francis">Coat of arms of Pope Francis</a></div>
<table class="wikitable collapsible collapsed" style="width: 100%">
<caption>Arms of Pope Francis</caption>
<tr>
<td><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Insigne_Francisci.svg"><img alt="Insigne Francisci.svg" data-file-height="1120" data-file-width="800" height="308" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Insigne_Francisci.svg/220px-Insigne_Francisci.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Insigne_Francisci.svg/330px-Insigne_Francisci.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Insigne_Francisci.svg/440px-Insigne_Francisci.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a></td>
<td>
<dl>
<dt>Notes</dt>
<dd>Pope Francis' initial <a href="/wiki/Grant_of_arms" title="Grant of arms">grant of arms</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Holy_See" title="Holy See">Holy See</a> was as <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Buenos_Aires" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Buenos Aires">Archbishop of Buenos Aires</a>, when he was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cardinal_Bergoglio" title="Cardinal Bergoglio">Cardinal Bergoglio</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NCR_178-1"><a href="#cite_note-NCR-178">[173]</a></sup> in which the depiction of the Star and Spikenard were <a href="/wiki/Tincture_(heraldry)" title="Tincture (heraldry)">tinctured</a> <a href="/wiki/Azure_(heraldry)" title="Azure (heraldry)">Azure</a>.<br/>
Following his election as <a href="/wiki/Pontiff" title="Pontiff">Pontiff</a> these are now tinctured <a href="/wiki/Or_(heraldry)" title="Or (heraldry)">Or</a>. The first version of <a href="/wiki/His_Holiness" title="His Holiness">His Holiness</a>' arms released by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vatican_Press_Office" title="Vatican Press Office">Vatican Press Office</a> depicted a five-pointed Star from Bergoglio's archiepiscopal version, but upon election as <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Pope</a> his <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> assumed an eight-pointed star with the representation of the spikenard also being suitably differenced.</dd>
<dt>Crest</dt>
<dd><i>Not applicable to <a href="/wiki/Prelate" title="Prelate">prelates</a></i></dd>
<dt>Helm</dt>
<dd><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MitreBenedetto.svg"><img alt="MitreBenedetto.svg" data-file-height="305" data-file-width="280" height="38" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/MitreBenedetto.svg/35px-MitreBenedetto.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/MitreBenedetto.svg/53px-MitreBenedetto.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/MitreBenedetto.svg/70px-MitreBenedetto.svg.png 2x" width="35"/></a> <a href="/wiki/Mitre" title="Mitre">Bishop's mitre</a></dd>
<dt>Escutcheon</dt>
<dd><i>Azure on a Sun in Splendour Or the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Name_of_Jesus" title="Holy Name of Jesus">IHS Christogram</a> ensigned with a Cross Paté fiché piercing the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Name_of_Jesus" title="Holy Name of Jesus">H</a> Gules all above three Nails fanwise points to centre Sable, and in dexter base a Mullet of eight points and in sinister base a <a href="/wiki/Lavandula" title="Lavandula">Spikenard flower</a> Or</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-451"><a href="#cite_note-451">[442]</a></sup></dd>
<dt>Motto</dt>
<dd><i><b>MISERANDO ATQUE ELIGENDO</b></i><br/>
(<a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> for "<i>BY GIVING MERCY AND BY CHOOSING</i>")</dd>
<dt>Other elements</dt>
<dd><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Keys_of_Peter" title="Keys of Peter">Keys of Peter</a> behind <a href="/wiki/His_Holiness" title="His Holiness">HH</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Escutcheon_(heraldry)" title="Escutcheon (heraldry)">shield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mantling" title="Mantling">Papal mantling</a></dd>
<dt>Symbolism</dt>
<dd>(On the shield) <i>Jesuit emblem</i>: In reference to Francis being a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesuit" title="Jesuit">Jesuit</a>, the uppermost charge on the shield is the emblem of the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" title="Society of Jesus">Society of Jesus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OR_452-0"><a href="#cite_note-OR-452">[443]</a></sup> This <a href="/wiki/Charge_(heraldry)" title="Charge (heraldry)">charge</a> displays a radiating sun within which is the <a href="/wiki/Monogram" title="Monogram">monogram</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Name_of_Jesus" title="Holy Name of Jesus">Holy Name of Jesus</a> in red, with a red cross surmounting the <a href="/wiki/Christogram" title="Christogram">H</a> and three black nails below the <a href="/wiki/H" title="H">H</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OR_452-1"><a href="#cite_note-OR-452">[443]</a></sup> <i>Eight-pointed star</i>: a long-standing symbol of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virgin_Mary" title="Virgin Mary">Virgin Mary</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Spikenard" title="Spikenard">Spikenard</a></i> alias nard: this flower represents <a href="/wiki/Saint_Joseph" title="Saint Joseph">Saint Joseph</a>; in <a href="/wiki/Hispanic" title="Hispanic">Hispanic</a> iconographic tradition St Joseph is often depicted holding a branch of spikenard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-VIS_453-0"><a href="#cite_note-VIS-453">[444]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Papal_coats_of_arms" title="Papal coats of arms">Papal coats of arms</a></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_album">Music album</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wake_Up!_(Pope_Francis_album)" title="Wake Up! (Pope Francis album)">Wake Up! (Pope Francis album)</a></div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Wake_Up!_(Pope_Francis_album)" title="Wake Up! (Pope Francis album)">Wake Up!</a></i> was released on 27 November 2015 and contains speeches by Pope Francis and accompanying music, including rock music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-455"><a href="#cite_note-455">[446]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-456"><a href="#cite_note-456">[447]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Press reports have provided a variety of translations for the phrase. According to <a href="/wiki/Vatican_Radio" title="Vatican Radio">Vatican Radio</a>: "Pope Francis has chosen the motto <i>Miserando atque eligendo</i>, meaning lowly but chosen; literally in Latin by having mercy, by choosing him. The motto is one Francis used as bishop. It is taken from the homilies of the <a href="/wiki/Bede" title="Bede">Venerable Bede</a> on <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Matthew" title="Gospel of Matthew">Saint Matthew's Gospel</a> relating to his vocation: 'Jesus saw the tax collector and by having mercy chose him as an apostle saying to him: Follow me.'"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Pronunciation: <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Spanish" title="Help:IPA for Spanish">[ˈxo̞ɾxe ˈmaɾjo β̞e̞ɾˈɣ̞oɣ̞ljo̞]</a></span> (Spanish), <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Italian" title="Help:IPA for Italian">[berˈɡɔʎʎo]</a></span> (Italian)</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-45"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-45">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This devotion has since spread to Brazil; it "attracts people with small problems".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[41]</a></sup> Bergoglio had an image of Mary Untier of Knots inscribed on a chalice he presented to Pope Benedict XVI in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[42]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-134"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-134">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">One source says that the <a href="/wiki/Gospel" title="Gospel">gospel</a> was chanted in Greek during the pope's inauguration Mass in recognition of Bartholomew's historic attendance,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-patriarch_131-2"><a href="#cite_note-patriarch-131">[128]</a></sup> but the Vatican News Service paraphrased <a href="/wiki/Federico_Lombardi" title="Federico Lombardi">Federico Lombardi</a> of the Vatican Press Office as explaining that "[t]he Gospel will be proclaimed in Greek, <i>as at the highest solemnities</i>, to show that the universal Church is made up of the great traditions of the East and the West." (emphasis added)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[130]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-140"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-140">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">31 October 2016 is the 499th anniversary of the start of the Reformation.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-216"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-216">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_I" title="Pope John Paul I">Pope John Paul I</a>, elected in 1978, took a new combination of already used names, in honor of his two immediate predecessors, <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_XXIII" title="Pope John XXIII">John XXIII</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pope_Paul_VI" title="Pope Paul VI">Paul VI</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[210]</a></sup></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-276"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-276">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">italics added to refer to English translation of the Latin motto</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-349"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-349">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Both in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Catholic_Churches" title="Eastern Catholic Churches">Eastern Catholic Churches</a> and in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Churches" title="Eastern Orthodox Churches">Eastern Orthodox Churches</a>, married men can be ordained to the priesthood, but priests cannot marry after having been ordained. See <a class="external text" href="http://www.vatican.va/holy_father/john_paul_ii/apost_constitutions/documents/hf_jp-ii_apc_19901018_codex-can-eccl-orient-2_lt.html#TITULUS_XVI" rel="nofollow">Code of Canons of the Eastern Churches, canon 795</a></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-425"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-425">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pope_Emeritus_Benedict_XVI" title="Pope Emeritus Benedict XVI">Pope Emeritus Benedict XVI</a> did not do this during his eight-year reign from 2005–2013; his predecessor, <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a>, married a group of couples from all over the world in 2000, as part of the Jubilee for Families, and before that in 1994 during the Church's Year of the Family, as well as presiding over a number of private marriages as Pope. All three conducted wedding ceremonies as cardinals.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-424"><a href="#cite_note-424">[416]</a></sup></span></li>
</ol>
</div>

<li id="cite_note-127"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-127">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web">Wooden, Cindy (25 January 2016). <a class="external text" href="http://www.catholicnews.com/services/englishnews/2016/pope-asks-mercy-pardon-for-ways-christians-have-harmed-one-another.cfm" rel="nofollow">"Pope asks mercy, pardon for ways Christians have harmed one another"</a>. <a href="/wiki/Catholic_News_Service" title="Catholic News Service">Catholic News Service</a><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">27 January</span> 2016</span>. <q>After walking across the threshold of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holy_Door" title="Holy Door">Holy Door</a> with an Orthodox metropolitan and an Anglican archbishop, Pope Francis invoked God's mercy upon divided Christians and apologized for times that Catholics may have hurt members of other denominations. "As bishop of Rome and pastor of the Catholic Church, I want to beg for mercy and forgiveness for un-Gospel-like behavior on the part of Catholics against Christians of other churches," the pope said Jan. 25 at a prayer service concluding the Week of Prayer for Christian Unity. "We ask most of all for forgiveness for the sin of our divisions, which are an open wound on the body of Christ," Pope Francis said. "At the same time, I ask all my Catholic brothers and sisters to forgive if, today or in the past, they were hurt by other Christians," he said. "We cannot erase what happened, but we do not want to allow the burden of past faults to continue to poison our relationships."</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3APope+Francis&amp;rft.aufirst=Cindy&amp;rft.aulast=Wooden&amp;rft.btitle=Pope+asks+mercy%2C+pardon+for+ways+Christians+have+harmed+one+another&amp;rft.date=2016-01-25&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.catholicnews.com%2Fservices%2Fenglishnews%2F2016%2Fpope-asks-mercy-pardon-for-ways-christians-have-harmed-one-another.cfm&amp;rft.pub=Catholic+News+Service&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>

<li id="cite_note-327"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-327">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Transcript of 2010 judicial inquiry, "<a class="external text" href="http://www.abuelas.org.ar/material/documentos/BERGOGLIO2.pdf" rel="nofollow">Bergoglio Declara ante el TOF N<sup>o</sup> 5</a>," translated in <cite class="citation" id="CITEREFIvereigh2014"><a href="/wiki/Austen_Ivereigh" title="Austen Ivereigh">Ivereigh, Austen</a> (2014), <i>The Great Reformer: Francis and the Making of a Radical Pope</i> (Kindle ed.), New York: Henry Holt and Co., locations 1897–1903, <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-62779-158-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-62779-158-8">978-1-62779-158-8</a>, <q>The option for the poor comes from the first centuries of Christianity. It’s the Gospel itself.
